O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, most dear son, I have completed this book which is the final part of the science of medicine along with its fulfillment, and I have reached the end through its explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of hands is rejected in our region and is foreign in every way, thus the science is lost and diminished, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this come errors and vanities, and intentions are closed off and science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 Or it seems to me that I want to enliven this treatise together with its arrangement according to the method of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the shapes of the cautery irons and other tools of the work with the joining of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And for this reason that no good masters of the art are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, and their movements and rests, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 Et pour cela dit Hippocrate que le nom avec le nom est beaucoup, et avec l'œuvre est peu; et de même dans l'art de la main.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 And we tell you in the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above should guard against falling into error and harming people; as I have often seen many who engage in this science and abandon their own knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 Because I saw a foolish physician who cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he cut into the arteries of the neck; because of which so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 And I saw another physician who removed a stone from a man with water, and the stone was large; so he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to remove it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew that if it was cut out, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And saw another doctor who took care of the Duke of our land, whose leg was broken and with the break came a wound; and the doctor, full of ignorance, reset the break over the wound at the bones with great force, leaving no space for air in the wound, and left it thus for a time; and commanded that it should not be unbound; and so remained until the leg became completely swollen and the foot, and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to go to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I unbound it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But all the same, the corruption was already established in the limb and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And thus another doctor who opened an abscess caused it to fester, and then set it on fire by the evil of his mastery.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For a cancer, when it is purged of black bile, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can completely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: that is to say, the work where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 For this reason, it is necessary that you protect yourself, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you. Therefore, take your arms in confidence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised; and leave the terrible diseases of serious illnesses; and remove your arms from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen said in one of his admonitions: "Do not take on a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and cold medicine cautery, and the chapter is arranged from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and the iron tools for cautery, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is arranged and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar things; and it is arranged from the head to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 Just as we recall the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest speech and most subtle science and secret response; and many of the wise have spoken about this and agreed upon it; but their words suffice me little, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 I say that fire cautery universally helps all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 In hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have debated and said that fire is of great help; and others said the opposite: that fire is of no use against diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 For the nature of fire is hot and should not be used to treat hot diseases by heat nor by dryness; and he who said the opposite said that fire is of great help against hot and dry diseases in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 When you examine the body of the man and his moisture in relation to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 Yet nonetheless, let no one interfere with this except for those who have experienced it, and who know through long practice the art of cauterization, and the diversity of men's complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the outcomes and the duration of time; we have no fear of other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that cautery with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 Because fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is burned, unless it can be prevented.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Burning medicines spread from one member to another and bring serious illnesses to the members; and by chance they kill the patient. Fire, because of its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, unless there is excessiveness.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 And thus I have found by experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself from the length of the speech, because it does not please me to take away the secret that is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out the diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed upon what time the cauteries should be done, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the harm that occurs is remedied by the aid of cautery; and likewise if the cautery is necessary for pain, it must be done quickly and urgently, before greater harm comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And do not ever think of it this way, dear son, as the foolish physicians do; for a disease that is healed by cautery does not return; and they say so; but it is not as they believe, because cautery is nothing more than medicine which moves the complexion, dries the humors that cause pain, and is more effective than medicine due to its speed of action, and the power of its work and dominion.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it is possible that the illness comes at times according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the illness and its power; and superfluities are gathered in him through the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in the place where there is little superfluousness and moisture, such as tooth cauterizations for pain, and similar things. And such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worthwhile after medicine, but their intention is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any illness and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cautery with gold instruments is more effective than iron, and they said this not foolishly but because of the quality of gold and the excellence of its substance; and they said that the place of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true for I have proven it, and I have found that it is true in some cases; and cautery with gold is more effective than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 However, when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly; and if it is heated too much, it melts in the fire; and thus there are many obstacles.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 Et pour cela nous utilisons la cautérisation au fer que nous avons préparé pour notre travail.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 And I have ordered this chapter from the head to the feet, so that it may be easier to find the vein.
dou cautere olivaire	 of the cautery for the eye
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is used for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two reasons for it: one is due to an illness called "soda," and the other is due to various humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and because of numerous dreams and toothaches and throat pain, and especially for all illnesses that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a solvent medicine cleansing the head III or IV times, according to what the virtues and the age and the custom of the patient can bear; and then make the back of the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And then have him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on a heavy weight; afterwards, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and where your fingers will meet, let it bleed from there, then heat the cautery which is called "olivare", of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the marked spot, and in descending and pressing your hand little by little while turning; then lift your hand immediately, and check the spot if you see the bone I inch; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take a pinch of salt, and put inside soft cotton, and place on the spot, and leave it for III days; then place a moistened cloth in butter; and leave it on until the burn is gone; afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and therefore, it helps to move (the body).
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of them said that one must let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what has been burnt from the bone, and it should be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And others say that one must let the cautery burn until it removes part of the bone, and press so hard that one removes a piece of bone as large as a spindle, which women use in their distaffs, so that the humors are moved out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards, one should cure and suture it.  />
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two types of cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is fear; and I think that I should leave it; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we prove in other members; and likewise when the patient's head is naturally weak, and the first appearance of cautery seems safer and more beneficial to me, I use this work together with salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 Of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When chronic pain comes to the whole head and lasts long, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and of purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if one makes him the cautery that we have said before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care if the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize under this cautery a little that we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 Afterwards, make a cautery on each horn of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place that is called "vasselz"; and this place is where one puts cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be finer than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is its form:
dou cautere dou chief	 Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When sudden pain comes to one part of the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the eye is purged with purging medicines, and other treatments have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then make cauteries in two ways, that is, with cold medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery with cold medicine is such that you take a clove of garlic and remove the skin and place it on both eyes, then make an incision in the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can put the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it is placed, tie and bind it well and leave it thus for XII hours; and then untie it and draw strongly over the clove of garlic, and leave the wound thus for II days or III; then apply a poultice soaked in butter as much as possible.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 Après le cure d'ognement, tant qu'il soit sanez; et se tu veus si fai ceu d'aucunes medicines comburantes que j'ai escripes en un dosme de traitier des medicines comburans.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 Prens le bout del fer qui fu dez ove et en chaufler a grans flammes.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 Por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta man que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 After put cotton in vinegar water, and place it on the spot for III days; then put wet cotton in butter, and then cure the spot of inflammation until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare," do so at the tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	 of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you cure migraine as we have said before in the division of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery mentioned earlier in medicine and iron does not suit him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and then place it on the painful spot for about a line and a half long, and remove your hand once, and strain so that you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when one chews, and let the nerve only move as much as it moves, and let spasm not come to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where there is great fear both for the one who knows nothing about it and who is not a student or experienced; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you in place in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that this cautery does not suit the disease, and the patient is tolerant, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with a cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the ear pain from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When ear pain comes from cold, and one has worked on it with medicines that dissolve and other treatments as we have said in the section, and the pain does not change, then heat this cautery which is called "point", of which here is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Après that you have punctured all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and you move away a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place; and there should be ten points around each ear; then treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 Of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torture that should be cured by cautery is nothing other than those caused by phlegm, as we have said in the division of illnesses; and do not make any cautery on similar cases that come from dryness or paralysis.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you treat this type of torture that comes from the phlegm of idres and purges of the head and gargle, and if it does not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery on the healthy part, and make the cautery at the top of the ear a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger; and leave the cautery until half the curd is burned; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it resembles the cuirass we mentioned earlier, but it is a bit more subtle and the blade should be slightly larger; afterwards, treat the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, one in the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	 from lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large doses and purifying pills for the brain; afterwards, wash the entire head of the patient, and apply on the occiput the mustard plaster that is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If he is healthy thus, good; and if not, let him receive III cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, and let there be between each cautery II fingers' width; and treat as with the others, and if you see it gather, and the patient is enduring, give I cautery in the middle; and if necessary, II more on the two temples, and treat until it is healthy; and let the cautery be called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 The head should be cleansed of hair and what we have said before; then wash the patient's head, then give him a cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, and I behind, and III on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is enduring, and the disease is advanced, give IV cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be until the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand; then treat until he is healthy, and let the cautery be called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	 of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to modify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and willing to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is a child who cannot endure it, give him gargles and chew treatments to modify the brain often with good foods; after that wash his head in the middle, and there make a cautery as we have said before, and a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and willing, make cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When because of melancholy there are superfluidities or corrupt moists and thick phlegm, then use the caustic cautery as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if because of melancholy the superfluities tend towards melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify their brain, as described in the previous section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After washing the patient's head, make a linen bandage well-shaped like a circle, and place it on their head; and the patient sits cross-legged, and is held securely from all sides; then present the liniment, made with old ewe's butter, and warm it moderately by fire so that two fingers can touch it without burning; then empty the circle into the head, and leave it to cool; and do this for each patient once a week with good management until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 Where you see cauterization done by making several points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This manner of cautery softens the scalp equally; and then apply a piece of cotton soaked in butter and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	 of the eye socket
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When it first comes to the eyes through the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to cleanse the head, and protect it from all moisture, and make him sweat in the bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 Then command him to shave his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent is into both eyes together, or one if it is into one; and cut through all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then staunch it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des artères et à l’incision la prudence dont tu te serviras; et parfois on cautérise ou incise sous les deux os de derrière.
dou cors des larmes	 of the body's tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 When the tears of the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the surface of the head; and it is seen that this comes from cold phlegmatic excess, then he should do the cautery as I said at the beginning: one cautery descending towards the eyes, one cautery in the middle of the forehead, two cauteries on each temple, and two cauteries in the hollow beneath the two bones; and if there is further need, then cauterize wisely above the hairline with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 of the body tears inside the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient to drink three nights of cochies; after that, anoint his head and make a cautery in the middle of the temples; and make two cauteries of the cautery which is called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, one a little below the eyebrows; and beware of the artery that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the tissue of the eye is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	 because here is the shape:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if you see this, make two cauteries on the two sore places as long as the sores are; and do not leave your hand until the third part of the skin is burnt, according to what I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 Sometimes it happens that the hair of the eyes is converted to the eyelid, and pricks the eye, and one makes cauteries in two ways: that is, by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they are born and are equal, then put the patient in your health; afterwards, trace on the papery of the eyes a figure that is similar to the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then place moistened cotton with egg white and musk on the eye, then heat the cauterizing iron which has this shape:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, cauterize over the figure that you have traced little by little many times, so that the hair is burned in that place; and the sign of the healthiness of the work is that you see the papery retracted, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then place moistened cotton with butter until the scalding is gone; afterwards, continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if the hairs come after that, and the skin is softened then recommence the cautery on that same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize it so that the skin is raised to its natural place, and be even, and let not the hairs prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and vive chalz, each one .З., and grind them well together; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin of the eyes; and if the disease is in one eye only, then work in one, and if in both equally; and put moistened cotton below the eye with egg white; and let the patient's eye be in your hand and place your finger showing on the medicine, and press the bag and the egg white every time the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for he feels the biting as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the bite has passed, lift the area of pain, and observe if you see the skin raised as if it had been raised by the constriction of fire or by an incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not worked until your actions are equal and your eyes are focused; then place moistened cotton in butter until the burning heart falls, then treat the ointment site which is called «dyafenis» and others, until it heals.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you need to guard yourself well in your work with great caution that no medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hair pricks in the eye, then begin the treatment again on the place that has been softened by the paper properly, as you did before; afterwards, cure it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the leaf of the myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and do not answer the straight way for him who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 On the treatment of fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you apply cautery to it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Command the patient to place his head on your hand; and the minister should hold his head between your hands in such a way that it does not move, nor does he lower his head; afterwards, put dampened cotton wool in vinegar or juice of parsley on the eye; afterwards, heat the cautery which is thus: and it is shaped at the top like the quill of a goose feather, along with the cautery; if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent; but nonetheless, this one which is shaped is worth more for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Afterwards, press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, then open it, and draw forth the pus; afterwards, place a very hot cautery upon it, and hold your hand at the cautery near the tip above the eye, so that your hand does not burn; and put the cautery into the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you come at the beginning of the cautery to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, then restart the cautery again one more time, and another if you need it, and leave it for three days; afterwards apply a cotton cloth soaked in butter, and continue the dry treatment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a method of cauterizing a fistula that some of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Take for a fistula, and open the place; afterwards put in the opening one subtle thread as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 And they make it in the quantity of one .З. of lead; and hold your hand firmly on the camahan, and let the patient not move at all, until the melted lead runs to his eye; and one must put on the patient's eye a piece of cotton moistened in egg white or vinegar: the lead is thus placed at the site of the fistula, and heals wonderfully.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula has been healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then a hole must be made in the nose, and the fistula should be brought back into the body of the nose, as is appropriate in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	 cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Often occur ruptures in lips called "hair", and likewise in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you heal these ruptures as we have said in divisions, and the healing does not benefit, then heat a small cautery knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And put it quickly into those ruptures until it reaches the base; afterwards, treat the place with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the throat abscess
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, afterwards it putrefies and rots and is inflamed and becomes a fistula; and you heal it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards burn into the hole or opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the fire reaches the base of it, and in the surrounding area; and do this once or twice, afterwards treat it as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupt bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 of the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines and this does not work, then place the patient's head in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery in such a manner that you put a reed on the tooth; and put hot cautery inside quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterwards remove your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; afterwards have the patient rinse their mouth with salt water, and keep it for an hour and spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this manner the tooth that was moving is made firm, and the softened gum is restrained, and the moisture is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	 of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When tooth pain comes from cold, whether it is cold or true, and medicinal remedies are of no value, then there is need for cautery in two ways: with the cautery of butter and with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 Cautery with butter is such that you take cow butter and put the end in an iron or copper spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and moisten it in boiled butter, and place it quickly on the aching tooth and hold until it cools; and thus do often until its power reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see moist wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it so that the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a tube of iron or copper and it should be thick enough so that the smoke does not reach the patient's mouth. After heating the cautery, as its shape will come later, place it on the tooth and keep your hand steady until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then rinses vigorously; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a cautery from whatever head you wish, according to what you have the power to do; and this is the shape of the tube:
des scrophules	 of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 when the scrofula are from cold and damp phlegm, and do not yield to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery handle as described below, and let it have two openings for the smoke to exit; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it there for three days; and then put on a cloth soaked in butter until the burn is gone; afterwards, cure the place with ointments and dressings until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the hound:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When the moistures rise to the passages of the brain, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be voided with purging medicines; afterwards make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care that you do not go as far as the throat, but only burn for a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards, make another cautery at the junction of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be of the form we have previously mentioned; and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 When cough and brain disease are due to cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the disease is chronic, let him make two cauteries on the breastbone in close places; and another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery which is called "clavicle" be according to the form previously mentioned. ️
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you see, perform cautery by pricking all the cautery that is called "point" of which the form is thus described in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or thereabouts.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After treating the place according to what has been said before, and let the cautery be for three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because these cauteries are lighter, therefore you should do them in three quick strokes.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder's dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 Après soit soigné le patient sur son dos et sur sa poitrine; ensuite lève le cœur qui est dedans le tissu avec les doigts de ta main gauche; et si la jointure est disloquée en dedans, alors chauffe le cautère qui a deux nerfs à cet endroit-là.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and cauterize the heart until it pierces through to the chest, and three figures of the cautery will come together with four cauteries; and because of this, the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nerves, which is why the figures of cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the fineness of a silk thread, and this is the form of the cautery that has three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is adjusted onto this nerve, which is why there are eight cauteries for it.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 Then place the cautery on and crush with silk; then have the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated above, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the shoulder joint, or in many places by pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When in the stomach there are coldness and much moisture to such an extent that it strains his constitution, and he has many catarrhs, and the usual treatments do not help at all, then the patient must be turned onto his back, and extend his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 Of this after he makes three cauteries, one below the scapula of the foot through the quantity of a finger, at all the cautery clavicle, and two cauteries on the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is in three angles, and there is such space between them that they are not joined together when they emit pus; and let the cauteries be so deep that they reach the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without deviation:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cautery, prick and burn on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you wish of incense; then cauterize the entire cautery which is called "point.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the treatment we have had before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When there is pain in the liver due to cold, moisture, and large flatulence, which is greatly moved from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated for this as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him at all, then the patient must be cupped on his haemorrhois; and place three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, near the hypochondria, where the ribs of a man come; and there should be the thickness of a finger between each cautery; and the cauteries should be long along the body, and do not press too much with your hand throughout the cautery; and only half the head should be burnt, and the patient should be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and stretch out his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if you wish to cauterize these cauteries of the cutaneous area, if you are skillful and wise in this art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and do not let it reach boiling, for the heart is very delicate in that place, as you know well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain but not too intense; and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then, when this treatment should be done by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back; and then they prick around the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a grape, like this is its form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And cauterize with the iron until the heart is burnt, and it reaches to the spleen, so that all the inflammation is expelled; after the cure according to the cure of fevers until he is healed; and it is not necessary that for this cautery anyone should use the iron except one who has studied long in the art of medicine, and by whom few of these diseases have ever been suffered.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can work boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is better to leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries with roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize I cautery between the breastbone and the neck, and II small cauteries a little below in the part which is under the beard; and II cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, slanting backwards a little; and I cautery in the navel, and I other on the stomach, and I between the two shoulders, and II on the sides of the navel opposite the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make it openly as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancients say that a man uses a cautery similar to a razor, and heats it and places it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; and if the pain increases, as we have said in the liver's abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, either the patient dies immediately or a fistula forms that cannot be healed.
de la mice	 of the bladder
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you cure the bladder disease as we have said in the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three types of cautery that are all good.
