Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	 One of these methods is that you make three or four cauteries, lining according to the length of the bladder, similar to the liver cautery shape that we mentioned before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient lie on his back; another method of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two branches, as we have shown in the shoulder dislocation; raise the skin that is near the bladder, where the patient's rib comes towards the left, and let the lifting be according to the skin, according to the length of the body, and let the cauteries be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	 After that, he inserts the two inflamed nerves so that they come out from the other side, and then he draws them out through the cautery, and thus there will be four of them. And if you see, then cauterize all the nerves at three points.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	 After the treatment when it has exuded pus for a long time, and this is worth more than other treatments previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	 of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	 The cautery is not beneficial to those with dropsy, except in the manner which is called "ascites".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	 When you treat according to the methods that we have divided into sections, and your treatment is not effective, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the anus, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the bladder, two behind the back on the spine, and one in the breast; and let the cautery be very close to the length of the nerve.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	 After leaving the cautery open for a long time to let out pus, do not neglect the patient's care after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	 The form of the cautery for the belly should be like the one we have previously shown; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, as is indicated above.
de l’enfleure des piez	 of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	 When the feet are swollen in a patient with dropsy and are full of yellow bile, you should cauterize on the back of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and raise your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	 And do not enter too deeply, for this would draw forth the yellow bile, and let the cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	 Then make two cauteries on each leg at the ankle bone; and let the cautery be long, one below the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without curing, so that the yellow bile issues from it; then cure the other wounds as we have said.
de la menoison	 of the madness
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	 When belly upset comes from cold and moisture, such that the retentive and digestive virtues in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by other treatments; and you see the patient is strong and of great strength, then make one large cautery on the stomach as has been spoken of before, or a circular cautery. And four subtle cauteries around the navel, each cautery subtle, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	 And if you see abundant moisture and the patient is suffering, make a cautery on the armpit, and one cautery on each eye, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	 of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	 When the hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and they are old and consist of thick, cold, moist, corrupted humors, and if they have been treated as we said before with incisions and it does not help, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, those which are completely outside under the navel, making a triangle bit by bit, and one cautery underneath the buttocks two fingers; and if you think that his stomach is cooled and the food is not cooked, and you see the face swollen, then make one large cautery on the stomach as mentioned before, and another on the liver, and another on the bladder with all the cauteries open; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After healing the place until it is healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	 of the flesh that is called "thelul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	 When you cut thelul, heat up the cautery that resembles a razor, and then place it completely burning on the cut thelul; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the base of the vein from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of thelul, then cauterize each one as we have said; after the cure of beneficial ointments until they are healthy; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchatim, it will be more effective.
de plaie mal curee	 of a poorly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	 When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such an illness occurs that it cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	 When someone has a fistula and it becomes infected and emits foul-smelling pus, you should examine the entire fistula carefully and ensure that you know the entire length of the fistula.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	 Then heat the cautery that resembles a razor and insert it into the fistula according to the length that has entered, and repeat the cauterization until the rotten and corrupted flesh is burned, one, two or three times, as needed; and beware of burning the nerves present therein, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	 And if the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, then avoid these places, and do not perform these cauteries except in fleshy areas, and know that it is not without reason; afterwards treat the place until it is healed, and if the place is healed and the matters have been removed for a long time, then you may know that the place is entirely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is broken open, and the bone at the root is corrupted; and thus as one of these which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	 of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	 When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and from great flatulence, and it does not take on the nature of a woman, then you must make a cautery on the kidneys on both sides with the clavicle cautery that we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be III cauteries in line, and they will provide greater aid.
de la vessie	 of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	 When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then make a cautery on the part outside over the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on each side, and let each cautery be as long as the thumb of a man; and make one cautery outside the back, if you have need for it; and let the cautery be clavicle-shaped according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	 of the uterus
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	 When the uterus is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the periods are corrupt and their terms late; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary that one make three cauteries around the navel, as we have said in the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries outside the back; and let the cautery be clavicle-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	 Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	 When the viscous moistures descend to the pelvis of the hip, and for this reason it moves from its place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of separation is found visible, then you must cauterize the patient on the pelvis of the hip with a cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the place around the pelvis as it turns, so that the pelvis is inside the circle; and let the cautery be such as that which has been used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if this cautery is not available to you, then make three cauteries with a large olive, and let the cautery be as deep as all the hearts; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	 Of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	 When pain comes to the hip joint from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	 Afterwards, make a cautery; and the manner of the cautery is in two ways: that is to say, together with burning medications, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	 Fire cautery is in many ways, one of which is as follows: you make three triangular cauteries on the hip joint like this, and make each one deep and large, with the distance between each cautery the thickness of a finger, and let the cautery be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip joint, so that there are four like this:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if you see it, then cauterize with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the hip; but do so in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire hip, and all the thickness of the knee is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	 And this is the way one does in sciatica, when the pain is in the hip and does not reach the thigh or the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then make two cauteries there where the patient says the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers’ width, slightly on the left side; and let the cautery be sharp, and burn all the thickness of the knee; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize there where they feel the pain with three or four points using the cautery called "point.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	 And if needed, do it more; and if he knows that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make a circular or knife cautery, and be careful in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and cause more harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	 And I myself have seen many who made a cautery on the ankle of the foot, and left it so long that the entire leg became swollen, and the foot as well, and all the foot was destroyed and rotted away.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	 After a colic attack which led to his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	 And if the pain is in two places together, make a cautery in one and in the other, following this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	 And the wise say in the cautery of the hip, this is how it should be done. Make such an iron and let it be at the tip as thick as a dactyl's nail, or slightly less, and let there be barbs between the barbs, and let there be from one barb to another the space of a pea; and let the barbs be covered on two sides, and let them also be like nuts, and there should be a well-made iron handle. And this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And let it be heated until it is all red and glowing, and then place it on the hip of the sick person, and turn it on the healthy side. And cauterize once for one cautery, and leave it for three days; and then make a plaster of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the care of ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	 Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery for fear of its gaze, and if we see few who use it; yet this is one of the good cauteries, which can endure it, and there where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	 The burning medical cautery is such that you make the instrument as a grille in which descends the margin of the door, and let it be of bronze or iron with one long side, and in the height it should have two holes, and between each the size of the thickness of a finger; and they should be open from below and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	 Then place the box of the hip on the patient lying on his sound side, and then put your hand very high on the box of the hip; then throw between the two circles of the cautery which should be heated in the fire one handful, and let it stay there for an hour of time, and let the patient endure the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Car it finds cauterization just like fire; and when the cauterization has passed, remove your hand with the instrument and gently lift the hip; leave it thus for III days, and apply butter until that which is blackened by the burn is removed; leave it thus for III days so that the putrefaction may be drawn out; and this would be the final help after the treatment of onions until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	 And if the pain has spread to the thigh or to the leg, make an instrument that holds water according to what you have done on the hip in the same way; and this is the manner of hot water, and I have written about it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	 Take alkali and quicklime, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, then put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	 where there is a small hole outside so that the tip of a razor can enter; and put on top of this pot another well-plumbed pot, and pour on top alkali and lime and water as sweet as you can, until there are two hands’ breadths above the powders, which you will have held firmly in your hand; and let it sit like this until the water descends and collects in the plummeted pot, then take all that water, and pour it on top of lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	 And then it will be very watery and is prepared for many works of medicine and other members' cauteries because it does the same work as fire, and there are other medicines with which one can cauterize the hip well in this way, such as terebinth, honey, anacardium, lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	 And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of the pain of the hip and sciatic vein, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other cure was done for him, and that he was cured in one go after this cure was performed, and he bathed as he instructs hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	 And he says in this manner that you should take fresh and dry lead, and grind it very well with a little fat, and apply it to the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is, and let it sit; and leave it for III hours, until the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	 And then make him enter the bath so that his body is slightly warmed up, and put him to bed, and all the pain will go away, and he will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	 And know that no one should use such a cautery, unless it is after the evacuation of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	 And Dioscorides said that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with wool of goat, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	 Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe of the foot and the other one called phalanx.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	 Afterwards, take dry goat wool and press it into charcoal, and place it on the wool, and let it stay until it is burned; and do this again, and do not stop doing so until you think by sensation that it reaches the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "goat cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	 of back pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	 When pain comes to the back, from falling or striking it or from excessive evacuation, or from something like cold matter spreading out, in none of these cases is cautery valuable except for that which comes from the influx of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	 It is necessary that after the patient has been emptied by taking stinking pills or other similar things, one should make on his back where the pain is located three lines of incense, each line with five cauteries or more according to the virtue and quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cautery be done in the manner of the cautery called "poinçon"; and if you wish, do three or four cauteries of medium-sized cautery in this manner:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	 Many times this disease comes to small children, and the sign of its beginning is that they have a narrow groin when rising, and fear; and you find in the lower part of the back a spine that protrudes over the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	 When you see this and wish to cure it, then cauterize it with a hot iron according to this method.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	 So that the iron burns each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	 And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with a pointed iron that is two or three fingers wide, and let the points be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	 After curing the place until it is healed as we have said, be careful not to administer a cautery in an area of swelling that touches a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	 of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	 When the pain of the joints is due to moisture that spreads to every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which doctors call «podagre» properly, and when it is due to cold causes and the treatment of medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauterizations around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	 And if you need to puncture the surface of the foot, make a cautery all around called "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	 And if the pain goes up to the knees and other joints, which often happens, make three or four cauteries on each knee from each side, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand over it for longer than the length of a arrow.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	 And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	 And if the pains are in the hands, then make an incision around the wrist two fingers wide; and if there remains any pain in the arms, then make an incision on each joint and at the base of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ribs or to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and take good care of the patient and give him medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	 For if you take good care of him and you bleed him, he will be healthy with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	 Of the wound of the sinus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When the wound comes to the anus, and the bowels descend into the kidneys, which is new, it is necessary that when you see it being healed, that he does not eat on that day; and that he uses things that cause the belly to empty itself, so that the feces come out of his belly; afterwards, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his arm so that the bowels are repaired, and pull them towards you with your fingers, and sign below the wound on the bone of the wrist, and all at once, making a mark similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in this manner:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	 until he is white and casts seeds.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	 until he is healed and throws out pus.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	 And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	 And the cautery of children must be subtle according to their size, and for large people also as large according to their size; after three days, cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; then cure with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it must be that his nourishment is lengthened so that pus does not come out when he wants to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	 And after XL days, when he wishes to rise, if he wears a well-made bandage, and bears it for XL other days; and has good rest, that he labors little and guards against too great repletion of drink and food, and of too loud laughing; and when he follows this teaching, then he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	 And I will say hereafter the cure for cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	 of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	 When ruptures come in other abdomens and are noticeable, and you see that they do not grow more, make I cautery with the cautery according to its size, and let it be burned the third of the heart; after the cure as we have said; and some of the ancients have said one should cauterize it with a III-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	 but first mark the spot with ink and make a line along the width above the wound, and another on the opposite side, then place your hand in the middle of the entire cautery area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	 But the first cautery is lighter and softer.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	 due to old pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	 When pain comes to some limb, from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and medicinal treatment is ineffective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called "poin," and the cautery should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, strength, location, twisting, and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	 if it is healed from the first cautery, that's good; but if not, repeat another cautery on top of it, because it is customary for such things to change in the member that is closest, so you must perform as many cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	 of mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	 The mixtures are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and especially the illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	 Can you see her being cauterized? Take care if the illness is in its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither remains nor lingers, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head towards the crown, and the other towards the forehead at the hairline; and two on each temple, and one behind on the occiput; and hold your hand so that the cautery reaches to the bone, and so that the scabs come out such that the vapors of the thick humors can exit; and also cauterize on the nose according to what was said before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	 And if the poisoning is spread throughout the body; and it clearly worsens, then you must cauterize with these cauteries that we have mentioned earlier, and one cautery on the back of the neck, and two cauteries at the base of the skull, and six cauteries along the spine of the back, and one large one on the buttock and another nearby, and two on each shoulder; and two on each arm, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and in the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the lower back, so as not to burn them; sometimes a cautery is made on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	 And know that the more I do of cautery, the more I help him, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain in the cautery as the healthy ones feel it, because his body is already completely corrupt.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	 And it is necessary that the cautery be large or small according to the members and the joints, as you will find in the manner of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	 After curing, anoint the place with flour of vetch mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When swelling comes to any member and is cured by medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not healed, then I make cautery on the member according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little into the thickness of the skin; then cure it with onions until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	 And sometimes the cautery is done on the hand and on the foot and on the back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb; and thus the swelling is removed; nevertheless, let no one interfere with it unless he is knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	 of scars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the disease called "albaras" has been awakened, and the physician's remedies are of no value, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes; then cure with flour of peas and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of a pigeon and blood of an almond tree, one part each; and let everything be mixed together, and bound with a cloth, and left in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	 The cure of cancer through cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	 When the cancer first appears and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	 Nevertheless, the wise say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; however, this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen sometimes; and it is more appropriate that it be cauterized around [it], with the cautery that is called "circular," as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	 of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	 When someone has a disease called "dropsy," and it delays death either due to excess fluid or the thinness of the patient when he is decrepit (that is, too old) and has little blood, or because of time; and you see that it hastens death: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries, pricking [it]; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	 For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you see it burst through the entire cautery, heat the cautery with this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	 And place your hand in the middle of that illness called "adubelati" until the cautery pierces the heart, and let the cautery be such that the patient feels it outside in such a way that the course of the corruption is eased.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 After the treatment is finished so that it may be perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	 the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	 Another manner of illness there is which is called "corrodens," and it is nothing other than a gnawing of the member, for it gnaws at the members just as fire does dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	 Se tu vois cette maladie en un lieu qui puisse supporter le cautère avec du feu, alors chauffe les cautères claviles, tant petits que grands, selon ce qu'il convient au lieu où la maladie est; ensuite, cautérise de toutes parts jusqu'à ce que tu aies brûlé toute la corruption, et qu'il n'en reste rien, afin que tout ce qui est corrompu soit retiré.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	 And then leave it for three days, and put on the places that have been cauterized a poultice with oil until the burns from the fire are removed, and all the corruption is gone.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	 After the treatment of wounds producing flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	 And if after three days you see that the flesh does not heal, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted place.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	 And this lie is sometimes cured with cold medicine instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already said the remedy for cold medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	 From leeks that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	 It happens very often that on the soles of the feet, outside, there is a disease called "blister" according to our understanding, and it is a large warty thing that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	 And the cautery for this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	 That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	 Fire cautery is done by heating a cautery like a goose quill, made of good iron to the size that it can enclose the wart on all sides, and let there be fine edges; then place it very hot on the wart, and turn your hand completely around the wart until it reaches the bottom of the wart; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster of crushed wild mallows with linen, and let the plaster remain all night, and the wart will fall off and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat the place of swelling by applying a plaster until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	 And if they are turned outward on the body, and this often happens in hands and feet, then you must bring a cautery of hot water; and it is done in this manner: take a needle of brass or iron, or a feather of bird-of-prey, and place it on the nail and the wart, that is to say for common warts; and place the needle so that it pricks all around, then put a little hot water on it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand in turning so that the edge of the needle comes to the root of the nail, and the hot water can find a deep way to the root; and let the patient endure the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave him like this, and it will completely uproot all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	 So do one after another, until you have extracted all those that are in the body, then treat the wounds that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	 Cure the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	 When someone shakes from cold of the nerves, or from quartan fever or another cause, you must make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cautery; then the shaking will cease, and the health of the cold disease will hasten.
des pustules puans	 Of stinking pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	 Sometimes appear on the outside of the body, or stinking pustules, which come from large corrupted materials.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	 If necessary, as soon as they appear, a cautery should be made on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from mirte wood, with which the point is grasped by the fire, or a long root of aristolochia, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	 And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow from then on, but the superfluities from which they come are broken down, and they heal; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	 When the vessel is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	 Often there is a great outpouring of blood from the vessel that is cut in the wound that occurs afterwards, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very serious matter to staunch it.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	 And yet when this happens to someone, hasten to place your finger on the vein wound, and press very hard until the blood is stilled under your finger, and no drop comes out; then put into the fire several small and large cautery irons until they are all red; then take one, whether large or small according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place the iron on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the iron there until the blood is congealed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	 And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the iron is extinguished, then take another one hastily from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	 And do not stop doing one after the other until the blood is clotted; and beware that you do not burn the nerve next to it, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when the blood flows from the artery, it cannot be properly clotted, especially when the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by tightly tying with thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to clot blood; and let it be bandaged and bound appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	 Whoever administers clotting by tightly binding with cloth or applying hot things, or similar things, will not benefit if it is not beneficial.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	 And if this happens to anyone and he has neither physician nor present medicine, then he must place his finger on the vein of the wound as we have said, and properly extend it until it is congested over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it often with very cold water until the blood is frozen and swollen and congested; and make further inquiries regarding the cautery and medicines he needs.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	 Here begins the second book on the treatment of hernias
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	 We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases for which it is necessary to cauterize with fire or hot medicine, and the questions and causes and instruments and forms of cautery; and I have placed this chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter in the same way so that those who seek may find more easily what they wish.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	 Et avant que je commence, il est nécessaire, cher fils, que vous sachiez que dans ce chapitre, il y a plus de danger et de peur qu'au premier des cautères, et pour cela, il faut faire preuve de grande prudence.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	 For in the work of this chapter, there is often an evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	 And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	 Because many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	 if it comes from such people who have this with their illness that they die easily because of the madness that they experience from their illness, and because of the great evil of it; and one must fear these things.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	 And there are those who give you their sense, and say: “wait, I am healed”; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	 It is not fitting that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put greater caution in your honor than in your desire, and do not act foolishly but wisely with regard to what you are certain of, and from which you can take praise; and use prognosis and diagnosis in the treatment of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	 Very dear son, May our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, And if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	 Now I have ordered this chapter by discussing in chapters, according to what is before the chapter on cautery, which I have discussed with you from head to foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	 full of water from the top
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	 Know that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the midwife presses too hard on the child's head; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	 And I have never seen this illness except in children, and in all those that I have seen death was hasty; and for this reason it seems to me that I should leave the work of such cures. ‌
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	 And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the skull swelled each day until it could not support him; and the moisture grew so much that he died. And this moisture is collected under the bone above the forehead, between the brain and the bone; and the work is such that if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, you should make a wide incision in the middle of the skull.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	 If the moisture is more thick and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, like this:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	 And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the seams of the skull open on each side, and the water jumps out strongly when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond to you: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the skull like this:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	 And after the incision, draw out all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	 After drawing out the moisture, apply bandages and powders, then put wine and oil on it, and leave it thus until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound by tenths and ointments, and allow the head to be evenly bound, and give the patient dry food of little moisture until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	 And another way of incision is that you look at where the largest part of the abscess appears, and the gathering of pus; for sometimes it is in front; sometimes behind; sometimes on the right; and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	 Cut then the flesh where the abscess opens, and the filling of water, and the wound according to your ability; and beware that you do not cut the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from bleeding and moisture evacuation.
de reume	 from the back
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	 When it happens to someone that there is a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the bladder, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the final cure is cautery with which one will cut the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	 Therefore, when you want to cut the veins, let the patient bend his head backward; then rub the place with a rough cloth until the veins appear, then have the patient stretch his neck with all his might; then look where the vein beats, and the places of the one and the other are behind the ears, and they are few in number; then mark the places, then cut one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts, so that the cut reaches to the bone, and this should be as wide as the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	 Et si tu veux, mets le scalpel sous l'artère et coupe dessus, en tranchant ainsi comme il faut en travers.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	 And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts out continuously in a strong jet.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And if the artery is not open to touch, then it is necessary that you measure the width of three fingers, and then cut deeply down to the bone; and concerning how much blood must come out, it is six hundredths, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then examine the wound: if there remains a point on the bone that syphac, cut it so that these abscesses do not come in, then press the wound and bind, and apply ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	 of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	 When an old headache comes and acute catarrh, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and old foolishness and similar things, and he is treated by various cures of medicine and all that does not benefit him at all, we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of extracting them is such that the patient turns his head so that the hair on his temples is out of the way, and he looks for the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its pulsation, and it is little concealed except in some men who are too cold; and if it is hidden, then the patient should extract it with some linen cloths, then rub the place with a rough cloth, and bathe the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula of which there is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	 then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then draw it up to the pincers, and separate it well from the tissues beneath each part; and if the artery is subtle, then turn it with the tip of the hook, then cut that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	 For if it is not cut, then the blood will not flow at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	 And draw blood from the VI c/ until the III; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in two places with a strong double silk thread to prevent gangrene before the healing of the wound, and let the bleeding come out gradually; then cut the excess between the two ties at that same hour, and then, if you see fit, use the knife cautery until the bone, so that the fingers are amputated; and this is the best work if the patient does not have a fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	 Because the cautery is used to remove moisture: for this reason, it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	 When it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the place with old cotton and apply well-made bandages; and when they are removed, they should be treated with dry medicines that promote the growth of flesh, and with bandages, until they are healed; and if there is an exit from the artery as long as you work on it, quickly cover with copper by cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and hold in your hand until the blood is coagulated; and if you do not have this present, then press the place with your finger until the blood is congealed, and wash the place with cold water until the blood ceases, and hold as needed; and it is better and easier for the extraction of the artery to cauterize the vein with a cutting cautery from two parts, but the cuts should be well spaced to retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	 Because when the instrument is too blunt, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And there should be one finger's breadth between the two knives, and then when you have incised in two places, and you place the hot iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let the two heads be far apart because this cautery is not sealed at all; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	 tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	 When tears descend from the veins that are on the temple of the forehead, and medicine applied there is of no use, and you see the patient's face turning red, and feel trembling in the forehead; and the eyes are dull and moist so that the hair falls out, and the temples are heated and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this cure is necessary. ︎
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	 And the ancients called it «cure for contusions», and it is that you should make on the patient who has this disease, the hairs he has on his forehead, then make III incisions on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as if two fingers wide across the entire forehead, descending downwards to the nose, and the other two at the temples above the eyebrows, and beware of cutting the arteries that are at the temples above the eyebrows; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let each wound be the size of three fingers wide across; and have prepared a piece of sponge and many cloths for wiping the blood, then apply the sharp spatula in two parts from which the shape is formed:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.
