From the incision that is above the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the heart that is between the two cuts along with the fat that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second incision, and then extract strongly this spatula-like object.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 If you place the instrument called "cultellar" in the first cut, it is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 Place the cutting side towards the fat on the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous with what opens onto the heart, and then make another cut in the middle cut to the other side; and then draw out an equal amount of blood, and press the place for the taken blood; then put in each cut a piece of old cotton, and put on moistened cloths in wine and oil and garlic, and ensure that such abscesses do not come; and on the third day remove the bandage, and apply a large amount of warm water, then a basilicum ointment cure with rose oil, and other cures used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	 of the pain of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When acute catarrh comes to anyone, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakening the vision, and the eyelids burning; and the hair falls out, and there is a severe pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these symptoms that this material and this catarrh do not come from one vein alone, but many, and the cure must be as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you instruct the patient to shave their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one from the hairline down to the eyebrow.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when chewing; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton wool and linen threads between the two lips of the incision, then bandage on top with cloths soaked in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscesses; once it is removed, you must rub the bone until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying substances that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice; and administer it into these wounds to heal flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 of the suppuration of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grain, beast, stone or similar object such as iron; seed, such as peas, beans, lentils; or flowing substance, such as water and honey and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When something falls into the ear such as stone or other object that does not fit in the ear and cannot grow within the ear, place the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, drop some oil of violet or sesame oil into it, then administer extraction; and make him sneeze with condiments, and hold his nostrils when he begins to sneeze, and place cloths or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 When this cure is applied, festering often occurs; and if it does not fester, use subtle tweezers for the extraction.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 If it festers in the tweezers, that is good; if not, use a fine pincer with a small double blade; and if it does not fester from this, make a hollow reed and put the end of the reed strongly into the hole of the ear, and stop up what is around the reed with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the reed; then draw strongly for festering, because it often festers as we have said; and if it does not fester in this manner, take glue as birds use, and put it into some instrument that is suitable for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or whatever it may be, and draw strongly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it does not heal from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before an abscess or spasm comes, and the manner of the cutting is such that you first bleed the patient with a cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its power. Then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small incision at the root of the ear in the fatty area below; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 And if it is grain that is inside and swells, then administer an extracting ointment; and if it cannot come out, then administer a subtle emollient ointment in this manner.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this if you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it with subtle tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 In the case where water falls into the ear, it is necessary that the patient first sneezes forcefully and then fills the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let it lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps through the sky, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If not the sky, then take many stones according to the length of your hand, light and thin, and heat them slightly in the fire; and put one of these stones in the patient's ear where it hurts; then let him jump on his feet from the other side, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out, and so it jumps all out; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and hold the other end with fire until the longest part of the reed is burned; then repeat with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 In the extraction of an insect, if it is small like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use extraction by pincers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 In the extraction of maggots in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in dealing with distillations, and the treatment does not work, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if there appear any maggots, then extract them with fine pincers, and if none appear, take the cane of which this is the form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And press the most subtle part into the ear according to the intensity of the patient's suffering, then draw out all the wax; do this often until all the wax comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, then plug the ear with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not come out easily as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatment of distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this instrument, whose form is thus as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And whether of silver or copper, put under a small hole, and above a filter to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation, a well-made copper tool for this purpose; and if you wish, take a funnel and wrap around the tip some cotton evenly; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines in the funnel, and let the funnel be in the ear; then insert the funnel into all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the ear's opening; and the patient feels it inside, and let the distillation be a little heated over the fire before it is distilled into the ear; and see that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of the ear plugging
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any opening in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults by plugging of a wound, or by flesh growing inside the ear, and this plugging sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is not enough opening, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Therefore, the one that goes deep and cannot be seen is of great difficulty in many situations. And the one that can be seen must have the patient's ear placed in the sun; and look inside: if you see the hairy appearance, then work all this spatula with which it has the shape:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind completely, so that it does not injure the ear; if the incision is of the flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the incision is deep into the ear, take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly in the fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the incision where the patient feels pain to touch, pierce lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this each day until the wound is healed: take a linen cloth and soak it in rose water, then sprinkle vitriol powder on it. If you see the ear swell, it is necessary to remove the linen cloth and replace it with another soaked in cerate made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling has subsided; then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear; and use other treatments that stop bleeding which are described in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	 from paper skin
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 This althea that comes from paper skin when it is wet and then dried, must be stretched with tongs and tweezers, and scraped with a spatula made of its roots; then place powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 And if it is without skin, cauterize it with the subtle lens-shaped cautery; and let the cauterizer follow after the incision is made; and many times they return when any part remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, then those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	 of goose flesh
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times there come in the eyes things that seem like goose flesh in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is a large assembly of moisture in the upper and lower eyelids; the operation is as follows: watch if the hail moves from one side to the other, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision across it, then lightly scrape each part, then take it with tweezers, and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot close it without piercing the skin a little, it does not bother the patient; and if the cut is large, join it with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not use force, for the ointment restores it quickly and new flesh grows.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 And if the boil goes down into the ear towards the upper part, then peel off the skin, and stretch out the boil with tweezers, and close and press it from both sides; and if the skin is separated by the cut, it does not matter; and when the boil is closed, wash it with salt water, and treat the place where new flesh grows until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 Exinach is a fat that is incarcerated in the eyelids above, and this happens more to children than to any other people, and it grieves their eyes greatly, and catarrh comes to them in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason, they always lie on their faces, and sleep on top, and their eyelids below are moist where the inflammation and appearance have been covered by exinach that appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the place between your two fingers, you feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head in your lap; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach from each part, then place it on him; and press with both hands on either side, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp scalpel a cut of sufficient width, and let it not be larger than the wound one makes at the vein of bloodletting; and cut the skin deeply until you reach the exirnach; and in several positions comes exirnach from the incision, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 Extract all at once with a piece of cloth between your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is scattered; and beware that you do not enter into the cleft, lest you should reach all the way to the eye and injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 And if the pustule does not open at the beginning of the cleft, widen the cleft slightly until it opens; then extract it as we have said, and moisten cloths in vinegar and water, and place them on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are some men who grind salt and place it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if a hot abscess appears, then treat it with soothing poultices until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 When hairs grow on the eyelids other than their natural state and are neglected, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as tearing and softening of the lids and pterygium, to the point where it leads to blindness; and the treatment is in four ways: either by cautery with fire, or by medication according to what was said earlier in the chapter on cautery, or by incision and suture, or by canthus, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your hand, then turn the eyelid towards your left hand; if it turns, that's good; if not, insert a needle with all its thread above; and let this be near the edge of the lid where the hair grows near these hairs, and draw the thread above all the lid, and turn it to the razor; then make an incision in the part below the lid, below the adjacent hairs, entirely covering the spatula from the large tear duct to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the lid, then press on the lid a figure like a myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to raise the lid which is called in all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And for one who needs to cut a large amount of paper according to how the paper is softened; then make all the spatula over the two lines that you have signed, and begin from the great tear until small; and let one of the tears be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then put the ink into one of the two corners of the heart, then scrape off all the skin; then gather the two lips together with a seam of a needle to all one thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and let the superfluity of the threads dry on the two sorcerers with some gluing things, if you want to do this; and if not, then do not worry about it, then leave the seam and the threads for three days or four; then cure the wound without a seam with dry and binding things, because the paper revives at the healing of the wound and its union, but the seam is harmful (as the ancients say), and this work is without fear; and there is another way: which is to sign the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have told you, with three dry inks according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 then cut according to those who dominate over the small forces equally, according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 and if you do not have the power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and put it in the middle of the figure; and put another thread next to the large tear, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the leather over which you have sewn, as we have explained, then gather the two lips of the wound by stitching, and care for it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then calm it with cerate and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hair on the skin is turned: then you must use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one place or another is more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 The cure of the cankers is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper inside out according to what I have said, and then make two cankers by art, and two subtle ligatures as long as the paper and wide as the spatula; and cut off the two ends where you hold the threads; then subtly bring together one and the other on top of that which surmounts the eye's paper, and tightly bind the two cankers in the two parts; and leave it so for some days, and the skin that is bound will die and blacken and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it is delayed, cut it with scissors, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and the paper has been lifted off, the hairs will no longer grow; and this is the shape of the two cankers that you should make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 the work is such that you take a subtle needle, and into it put a thread of soft and subtle silk; then assemble the heads and knot them both subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the sheath another brief and subtle silk thread, and knot the heads of the thread; then let the patient place his head in your hand; and let it be near the sunlight so that the work may be clearly seen, for this is a subtle and small work, then put the needle all into the sheath in the root of the hair close by, and make it pierce quickly through the skin until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the sheath, and put that hair into the sheath, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out entirely through the sheath with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the arrow is removed and the hair does not come out with it, you will draw the arrow down along its entire length that you have prepared, until the arrow comes out through the hole above and you can see it with your eye; then you will draw out the arrow and the string, and close the eye and leave it closed for II or III days, until the hair grows in its place and the flesh rises; and if the hair is small, let there be I long natural hair accompanying it, and let it grow with that one until it is elongated, then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the eye's infection
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "alecrati" or the infection comes to the eye, it is of two kinds: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the manner of working on it is that you split that seam, and separate its lips, and place inside linen tents, and bind until it heals; and it is not necessary to use in its care things that dry out and tighten.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and wash it with water or ale and flax seeds cooked together, and melted onions in some oil, and wrap it in a tent, and cure it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 And the treasure of your care is that you guard against it healing according to its previous form; and these works that we have mentioned are nothing other than corrections for this disease, lest it return according to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 from the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease, which is truly called "axacrati", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wound and tear and cautery and similar things; and the way to work it is that you take a needle with a double thread, and prick the fleshy part from the left lacrimal gland to the right, so that the thread passes through two layers of flesh; then stretch the flesh over the entire needle, and cut off a spatula wide at one end.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the slit, and turn the paper, and make two slits on either side within the paper; and let the ends of the two slits be at the two corners of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter which has the name "Greek"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its edges are sharp beneath, from what follows the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them together with a wool thread; then follow the cure as we have said for softening medicines and compresses, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 Et si la maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, il convient que tu fasses une fendure plainne desoz les poils des papieres, selon ce qui est ci-devant; puis desevre entre les II livres d'une tente, si com j'ai dit; et doit on faire l'ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car ele est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout son pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme naturele; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu'il i covient d'ovraige et d'estrumens en plusors dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 From the suddenness of the stone
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When this adhesion happens to many men in such a way that the stone above is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is then necessary that you insert the tip of a razor under the stone, and lift it up; and hold it with tweezers, so that you cut off what adheres to the subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot suffer the too sharp spatula injuring the eye; and let your incision, from which you peel that assembly, be light, so that the stone returns according to its natural form; and all that assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye there is salt water, and raise it with fresh water, and of collyrium; then place between the stone and the eye a linen tent, and put on the eye wet wool abundant in egg yolk; and after three days use collyrium and suturing things until he is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the thumb of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 You should know that the thumb is of two kinds: one is like a hard sinew and the other is not nerve-like but resembles congealed white moisture, which cannot be grasped with pincers when touched by iron; both begin towards the upper eyelid and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of the incision is such that the patient places his head in your hands, then closes his eyes; and you lift the skin with your hand, then twist the thumb with small pincers, and hold it up; then take a needle, and put in it one horse hair, or cow, or ox, and a strong thread; and bend the point of the needle a little and place it in the middle of the thumb, and pierce all the way with the needle, and tie the thumb with a thread and hold it up, and scrape off all the skin on the side of the thumb following the pustule and the thread to the root, then cut off the remaining part in the root of the eyelid with a very fine spatula and small forceps, and leave the natural flesh in the eyelid, so that through the incision does not come the body of tears as usual; and sometimes they are stretched only to the nail bed, and to the thread, as we have said; then you scrape off all the soft tissue from which this form is made:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And ensure that the sputum does not touch the fleshy tissue and break it, and that the plumule is not pierced; and after the incision, cast into the eye a little bit of boiled silk, and made from lead, and leave it until the next day; then cure what needs to be cured so that it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And if the nail is not fleshy, and you cannot insert the needle, and the cuticle cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicine; and as I have explained in the section on division, and if you see it covered, then work around the patient's eye, and take a little bit of sputum gently according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 And remove the nail from above subtly, and if you see that it is not diminishing and reason presses there, then drip from your mouth into the eye an irritant made of quicksilver and red columbine pounded together, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing is contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then let it drain, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 And if the appearance of flesh from the tear ducts troubles the eye greatly, then suspend it with a hook, and cut off part of it but not all, so that the body of tears does not come there; then drip into the eye red columbine made from quicksilver.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 Of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 Of the flesh that grows over some men’s eyes, there sometimes appears red flesh, covering the pupil and rising onto the eyelids, and turning them outward, resembling a baluster rose; and the work is such that the patient places his head in your hands, then you operate on the eyes, cutting all that flesh with appropriate scissors for this purpose, supporting it with forceps; then cut off the first layer of flesh, and continue cutting to the root with the scalpel until the end, taking care not to injure the eye during the operation; and let the incision be as we have said in the incision of the nail and in small forces from which the wax is removed, as shown in the following chapter of this treatise; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been cut away, fill the eye with cooled egg white to which you have added red colocynth and similar corrosive medicines, and place a compress of cotton soaked in egg white over the eye, ensuring it is secure against heat, and if anything remains and the pus overcomes you, and you doubt the heat, leave the eye and treat the inflammation with soothing remedies; then return to your work until it is healed, and do this whenever flesh grows in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 But nevertheless, you must alleviate the treatment of each weak eye according to its natural way; and for the accidental way, in ironwork; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is tolerant of such work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Which are red veins that cover the eye, and they prevent the eye from performing its function and weaken the eye every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 It is therefore necessary that you first look to see if the eye, in which there are such veins, is sound and has no other disease besides the veins; then treat the eye in this way: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then suspend those veins with a thread according to your skill, and let the thread be thin and doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 And let there be two small ones by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 then, as the forces of those subtle veins are coiled, and wipe away the blood hour after hour, until you see those veins withdraw from the eye; and be careful not to hurt the eye with the points of the spatula, and perform this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, distill into the eye green and red choler to corrupt what remains of the black.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	 And if you cannot coil all of them in that hour, then make a poultice on the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and the abscess is securely warm, then begin again according to this manner which is before, until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	 Of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 The surgeons name it «arissati» fistula: when you cure it by cautery and by burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a swelling in it that you should incise over the abscess, where it must be killed, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, draw it out with all the instrument as its form is here; and it is called «aspre chief», and let it be made of iron or steel, and let it be pointed like a file as it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And place above the site of the rotten bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is dried; and do this several times, then apply the site with drying medications.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the site is healed and flesh grows there, and the body of the wound is healed, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not reopen nor become infected with mischief, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other remedy than to bring back the fistula to the peritoneum according to this form: and it happens that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take an awl as follows, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the shaft be tapered to the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye socket. Then turn the awl completely until it pierces the bone, which the patient will feel due to the air escaping if he holds his hand over his nose; then restore the place with dry medicines as I have taught you. And when the flesh grows and the place hardens, the material goes towards the nose; this is an easier thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the eye is completely open in every respect and there is no obstruction or narrowing of the nose, it is necessary to bandage the patient; then heal it, then place cupping glasses without pricking to draw out, then place on the eye a plaster made of alum, aloe, frankincense, and myrrh, and then bind the eye, and cover with plasters and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is such that you take very soft cloths, and double each one four times, and then place one on top of another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then bind it tightly on top with a strong bandage, and reapply the cupping glasses to draw out without pricking; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bound day and night, and if the plaster softens, it is necessary to bind it very much; then remove the plaster after one day and one night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then reapply the plaster and the cloths and the plaster and the cupping glasses until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 Of the breaking of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 When disruption comes to the vein and it opens, and exudes papers like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; then if you want to cover it, the work is such that you insert a needle into the root of the part below until reaching above, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the lip; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cover the place of the double thread and tie a part of the vein around it, and hold it tightly, then withdraw the needle and place a wet cloth soaked in egg on it; and leave it until the thread adheres with the vein, then heal the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restricted by the vein every part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the eye gives off great appearance, then pierce it with a subtle spatula that comes to the bottom of the eye, and let the turbid moisture descend from the eye, and it will enter immediately; then draw it out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but water that is gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and this is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take the head between your hands on two sides, and move it until you see the water come to the surface before your eyes; then let it be pricked, and do not let it descend, and let the light be restored, and let the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the water is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 if the patient sits between your hands, then take a fine spatula and make an incision on the horny tissue in the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny tissue and the cornea, until the humour comes out; and when it has come out, instill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or boiled fenugreek water and honey, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the water of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have the appearances of the waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; so work according to the healthiness.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, outside the light for the sun, and tie up the sound eye very tightly; then place the eyelid of the sick eye in your left hand if it is a left eye, or in your right hand if it is a right eye; then take in your right hand, if it is a left eye, the instrument that is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if it is a right eye; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray into that whiteness of the eye at the lower part of the minor lacrimal duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" vertuously, and turn your hand until it pierces the whiteness of the eye, and feel that the almagda comes to the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of the almagda be at the fullness of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness; and this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in that eyelid by the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument in its place where the water is, then press under a way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If water enters now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After resting for a little while, and if the water rises again in the second path, put the fire with the instrument, and when it is firmly implanted and it does not rise, gently extract Almagda by turning your hand little by little; then place the eye back into the water for a moment.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then put on the outside of the eye wool or cloth soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind it with healthy skin.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, use comfrey with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if Almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument that is called "alberit," which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And pierce then the conjunctiva alone, and do not go too deep, but make the place subtle; then put almagda there, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which he sleeps on his back in a darkened room; and let him be free from all movements, and let him take light food, and let him not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him be bound according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 if the abscess comes to an eye, release it on the seventh day and apply the remedy that soothes abscesses; and when it is calmed, then release the eye and place a golden ring over its face to cover for some days, and let it always be in that darkened room.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then come out of the house little by little, and let it return to its usual activities; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And one came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almagda, for which they draw water, but nevertheless I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, pour ceux qui ne les connaissent pas les reconnaissent; et qu'elles soient de bronze pur.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And the head of these should be of the same subtlety, and the base in three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	 on the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes hairs grow on the nose in various arrangements, some of which resemble many-legged scorpions; and there are such that have red hair, and others have soft hair of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case, for the soft hair and not the red one, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open his nostrils and throw the incense onto those hairs and pull them out; then cut with a sharp, thin scalpel what you can support, until you know that all the hair is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if there remains anything that cannot be cut off, open it all with subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if without your help, or abscess occurs, then provide assistance as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the blood is staunched and all the flesh removed, then apply neat oil and vinegar in wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If pus forms and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as needed, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, which prevents the instrument from cutting: then you must insert a thread of linen, about a finger's width thick, and knotted by hand, with a distance of a thumb or less between each knot; and let the patient place the end of the thread in his nostril as much as he can, and pull while smelling until it comes through the nose into the mouth; and many children do this at school, and it is an easy thing for those who want to do it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and tie each knot in turn as shown by us who are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this so that you know the knots have corrupted that flesh, then draw out the thread, wipe off the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all that remains of the flesh; and then put a lead probe in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if dry medicines are needed, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, into which one distills the oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And let it be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp like a probe, and the channel likewise; and if you wish, make a closed probe, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; and have one handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 Of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 Often a disease called "telul" appears on the tip of the nose and grows large, so much that it is an unsightly thing to behold; and for this reason you must cut it at the beginning and remove all of its strength, then apply cautery or burning medicine onto the spot; and if it is delayed from being cut until it becomes large, beware if it is hard, of a dark color, and with a poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that it can be entirely removed, then the patient should empty themselves and cut without fear, and treat the area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nose is cut and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution of continuity comes to one of these cartilages in operation, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore when this happens to anyone, consider if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then join the two lips together in a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, then you must cauterize all their edges until they heal, then join the two lips together in a suture, and hold them, and put over powder of dragon's blood and pounded incense; and place over the powders a piece of strong emplastrum or other adhesive emplastrum, and leave it until it softens by itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	 The manner of sewing is that you join the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have shown you.
des apostemes des levres	 Of the abscesses of the lips
