A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many men have hard abscesses inside the lips, resembling barley grains, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lip, and cut over each knot, and take it with tweezers and chop in each part; then fill the place after the vitriol incision with broiled lime until the wound is blackened; and then apply honey plaster, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 Of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Often arises on the gums a flesh that is close together, which the ancients call "albulus"; therefore, you must hold it with pincers, and cut it at its root, and let the wound or blood flow; then place on the spot vitriol powder, or other restraining and desiccating powders; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it a second time, and cauterize: after the cautery it does not return; and these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 from sordid things
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Sometimes there are scales gathered at the tip of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; sometimes the teeth turn black and yellow and green, until the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head be in your lap, and scrape the teeth or the scales until nothing remains; and do the same with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellow discoloration and other stains, until they are cleaned away; and know that the teeth require different forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used on the outside of the teeth have other shapes than those used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you treat a tooth from its pain, you delay extracting it as long as possible, for one should never do this; for it is a very high substance to the point where there is no excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is forced to extract [the tooth], you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often the pain deceives the patient and he thinks it is in the healthy tooth, and he has the good tooth extracted; nevertheless the pain does not depart from him until the evil one is removed, for we have already seen this happen with these sages. And when you are certain of the aching tooth, then it is necessary that you burn around the tooth on all sides with a very strong cautery to protect the gum; then move [the tooth] with your fingers or with fine pincers little by little and bit by bit until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the pincers in place. And let the patient’s head be between your knees, and hold him so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out forcefully, then take one of these instruments and gently push it inside each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is decayed and rotten, then you must fill it with cloths where the holes are; and hold it delicately with tweezers so that it does not break while pulling; and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And be well aware not to break it, and leave a part behind, which would cause the patient greater pain than before due to the root's evil.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware not to act as the ignorant lords do, who sometimes out of haste and recklessness break the tooth, and do not bring those that we have mentioned, but sometimes cause great illness due to the remaining roots or the broken tooth, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood flows from it, which often happens, fill the place with burnt vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 Les formes des instruments, à quoi l'on arrache d'abord les dents, doivent avoir de longues pointes et de grosses poignées, afin qu'ils ne se plient pas lorsque tu tireras la dent; et voici ces formes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And they should be of thick members so that they do not bend during the extraction, and they should be made of well-forged iron, and they should have teeth to better grasp [the tooth].
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after extraction, you must place cotton moistened in butter on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the spot is softened, then put in the tweezers called "algefri", with which the tooth looks like a bird's beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and place there the instrument called "althali," which is plainly, of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 And let it be thick and large so that it does not break, and if the root comes out this way, it is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And also use this instrument that has two ridges, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other irons that are in front according to the teeth's reasoning, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, whose form is here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let this instrument be such that it cannot break; and know that many dental instruments are; and likewise other instruments that are not counted; and the wise master subtil finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients taught no instrument because of the diversity of others; and if one does not break the cartilage or other bones, where he can, he searches for the instruments he needs, which I have told you about, and helps with gestures, as the form here is.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not slip but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is rot in the bone, and it is small, then this instrument removes everything.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 When the teeth appear not according to the natural body, and their shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in its right place, and one cannot file or grind it: then draw it; and if it is near the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here, and it resembles a small beak, and let it be of very sharp iron at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the hook little by little in several days because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can file it, then file it with such a file as this form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 and it is also like the file with which one makes needles; and file the tooth little by little in several days lightly, so that it does not move until it falls out; then plane it at the end with any razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, you must file the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	 When the teeth dislocate
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the front teeth dislocate, either by impact or falling, and the patient cannot chew what he eats without them falling out, and you have treated them with binding medicines but it does not help; then they must be bound with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the width of the space between the teeth; and if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the thread and fold it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the knot between the dislocated teeth, whether there is one or several, so that you reach wisely up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the covering again until the place where you started, and gently and wisely tighten your hand so that it does not move at all; and let the ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then cut the heads of the wire with a pair of pliers, and assemble them, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and position it so that it does not injure the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can remain, and if it becomes loose or the wires break, then bind it again with another wire; thus it remains and serves this way throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the appearance of the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and skilled, and sometimes a tooth made from cow bone is fashioned, and placed in the place where there is a gap, and secured as we have said, and it remains and serves this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 of copper to bind the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Sometimes this ligament comes under the tongue naturally, in which a person is born that way; or by accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is such that you open the patient's mouth and hold his head against yours, and lift the tongue; then bind the nerve cord thickly until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is due to sudden healing of a wound, then insert the hook and bind the cord widely; and ensure that the incision is not too deep for the artery underneath; and when you have done this, lift the place with rose water and aloes, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen bandage; and let the patient wash the area every night to prevent it from healing.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding occurs, place vitriol on the spot to cauterize; and if the wound bleeds profusely, use the cautery with a slow fire, which is good for this purpose; then treat it further until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see the flesh turn black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it turns to pus, and there is moisture, sprinkle with oxide of copper, and pierce it with a fine spatula, and let out the pus from both sides; and if the wound bleeds during your work, place vitriol on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the force; then lift the flesh with oil and wax, and treat it further until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 From the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes there come within the throat pustules called "godath," and they are properly called two almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of red color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid bleeding; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you can divide it, or it will burst on its own; and if it is of white color again, and the root is thin, prepare the instrument for cutting, but first check if the abscess is warm and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his hands be on your chest, and he opens his mouth and takes the instrument between his hands, and presses the tongue down against the entire instrument, which has this form; and it should be of silver or fine brass like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 When you have pressed the tongue against this entire instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and insert it into the pustule, and draw it out strongly above more than you can; and some substance comes out with it, then cut off [or remove] the instrument, which has this form, that resembles tongs; and nonetheless the ends are curved, and one opposite the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this tool at hand, then borrow a pair of tongs, of which there is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And let it be sharp on one side and smooth on the other; and when you have cut off one of the tonsils, then cut off the other in the same manner, and afterwards rinse the patient's mouth with hot water and warm oil, and if blood continues to flow, then rinse the patient's mouth with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves have been boiled, and similar things, until the wound is healed; and then cure it until it is healthy; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them off in the same way as the two tonsils equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman with an abscess in her throat, specifically the abscess of little sense; and it had almost completely closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two veins through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened at once and placed one cautery in one nostril, then drew it out, and drained a great deal of pus from it; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I placed the cautery in those abscesses and drained some of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the throat of the woman was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not cease to cut from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess always grew back and filled the place that I had emptied, until it became very large again; then I lanced it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and know only what God did with her after me. etti
de l’uve	 of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the membrane descends to the grape, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cut as we have said in the division, and the incision does not help, and you see that the subcutaneous abscess is quiescent, and it is subtle, then you must cauterize it; and that which is round and gathered together is not long; and it is sanguineous or of dark color or black, then you must avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner I have said, of its color and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument which we mentioned before; then insert the onion into the grape, draw it down, and cauterize it with one of the two instruments which I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of the operation, then you must use skill in cauterizing away his fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of cautery is sharp and keen.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient should place his head in your hand, then press his tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the cautery chapter, and pour on it with sharp, living vinegar, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and fill the hollow of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And there should be on the head a sort of hair where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and the wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press on the eye, for a quantity of half an hour, until you see it darken and the biting of the medicine is calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above, so that the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and it will fall off after four or five days. And if you need to start the cautery of the medicine again, begin it again, and afterwards wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This cure is more effective than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamus and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in a pot, and put ashes in it, and boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument hung according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or bronze, and one of the heads should be placed in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nasal cavity, until the eye is inflamed; after that, repeat often, until the eye dries out, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, because many things happen there; and do not do it unless during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, take a dog and put inside its head an egg shell, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the egg shell does not allow the steam to bother the mouth, and this is a good treatment together with salt.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Often, a bone or fish spine becomes lodged in the throat, or some other thing. Therefore, you must extract what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with the instrument, so that you can move the object; and whatever does not open and is hidden in the throat, you should make the patient vomit before the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps the sharp object will come out with the vomiting. Or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of apple, or a lettuce root, or a crust of dry bread, then tie a string to the sponge and swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will become lodged, and then you can extract the string. And if it does not come out with what we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be curved at the top so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head raised upwards; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, for if the tool slips, it will come back, and do not push the bone inside; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because he knows where the hard parts are; thus he pushes downward, or draws it strongly with all the instrument equally, until it is strong.
de la sansue de la gorge	 from the blood of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the blood is treated with medicine, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you have pressed the tongue against the instrument that I have told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the bloodletting, draw it entirely with a small hook, or with subtle pliers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a hollow reed, and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the reed's tip, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient is thirsty all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full cup of cold water and pour it into the patient's mouth without them swallowing it, and move their hand over it often; and as soon as the bloodletting feels the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, using the instrument I mentioned for eye fumigations; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the manner of fumigation is such that you take a pot where there are hot coals, and the top is covered with a perforated cloth in the middle, and through that hole is the head of the instrument; then cast your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes up to the sinus; and the sinus will fall now, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and such, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to exit through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the shape of the instrument with which one draws blood is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pincers to enter the throat; and it resembles a bird's beak, and there should be roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave behind; and see here its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	 of the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Very many types of abscess are, according to what is remembered here after from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and it is in two manners, of which one is in its very nature, and of those that contain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is for the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 car the abscess on the head is different from that at the base, and the abscess in the fleshy part is different from that which occurs in the joints, and each should be judged accordingly in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such that must be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their nature, such as abscesses near the joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when abscesses come near the joints, and one lets them become rotten around, it may happen that the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contracture in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 In the case of an abscess near the principal member, and if you delay perforation until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; if it is near the fundament, pierce it as soon as it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce a ripened abscess before digestion is complete, except for one that is near the fundament, so that it does not putrefy deep inside and become inflamed, causing a fistula; and may not heal quickly.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 And it is necessary that you know the time of perforation for a ripe abscess according to completion, which is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of fever, and the lessening of pain and redness, and the debating and ripening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you perform the perforation in the most dependent place of the abscess, where it opens; and let the incision be along the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no flexibility.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, then the body will be filled with its poison, and it is full of much filth; and perhaps it will harden the lips and depths of it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there are any abscesses that have been pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limbs need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And you must bring in small abscesses, small openings; and in large abscesses, large openings, and many incisions according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where one must cure the head, and cover when it becomes like linen, and is dead, then you should do as one does with buboes: and there are such that are split into three angles, and there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the anus; and there are such where a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cutting.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it thoroughly; and when the abscess is large, and it has collected great pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out something again; do this many times over several days, until all the pus comes out; similarly if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit sometimes leaps with the exit of pus, so that by chance the patient may die, and you may not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, wash the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a plain cut, bring ten linens or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then you must put one tent into each so that they come together; and if you have cut into the abscess some part of the skin, and you have removed it, then you must fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and bind it up to the third day; then remove it, and cure it with oil until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, then prepare cold and clean water, and moisten the cloth, and apply it to the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, then bring management and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is in winter and the place of the abscess is very sensitive, then you must apply tents and cloths moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer and the place is fleshy, then you must apply cloths moistened in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then lance the abscess and dry and treat it, as needed, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 And it must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 Of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where small abscesses come from the head, and are like pimples that we have on our faces, similar to the down of a chicken.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some that are fat and such where there is moisture like a blister; and there are those which are hard and stone-like to cut, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not act against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you should try all the instruments which are called "spoons," from which the shape comes as described later, whatever it may contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 If it contains moisture, then cut through the top of the tendon.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is removed, scrape off everything without leaving any skin that contains the moisture, for it returns immediately if anything is left there; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and linen cloth, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and this will cure what remains of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then repeat the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, so that you know well that none remains of the night; then treat the wound with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess holds any grease, cut it in this manner, lengthwise; and throw away your nails, and scrape from all sides, and put all your care into drawing out the skin where it lies; and if the art of healing opposes you, then do as I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And likewise do with the abscess if it is hard, and in cutting and cleaning as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut above the hard and moist abscess, for it is lighter, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if any of these abscesses are at the head where there is no moisture, and of these were the abscesses that I cut at the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, and white stone, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it, one would have made a wound as well as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other boils that come on the head, except those that come on the heads of children and the roots of the ears, let the opening always be made in the lowest possible place so that the pus may flow out; and treat it as needed.
des scrophules	 from scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this boil occurs on the neck, under the armpits, in the groin, and sometimes in other parts of the body, and they are many and interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is properly within its rib, just like the nut and the boil on the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In that one which you see of good disposition to touch, and it is similar in color to the body, and moves from each part and is not close to the nerves of the neck nor the artery nor the vessel, and is not deep; then it is necessary that you cut above it, and skin it from each part, and extend the two lips of the heart to the corners, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the spatula be neither too sharp nor cutting, lest the hand slips, and does not go too far forward, lest you cut something that you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or some powders that constrict blood, and constrain the wound; and leave it until the abscess is appeased, and the wound becomes softened, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is constricted, then return to your work until you complete it; then test with your finger if there are any small scabs remaining, and cut them off and clean them away.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, it is not necessary to cut that scab at its root, but tie it off with a strong double thread, and let it fall away without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut all the scrofula, it is necessary to join the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since no surplus remains due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 it is necessary that you attend to cutting the root of it, and pull strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulae that have surplus, pierce there where it is visible to the eye; and pierce thus as said before, hanging downwards, then bring in tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, cure it with ointment enveloping flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	 of scorching
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and discussed the cutting of the throat; but I never saw anyone in our land who did it, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 For those who have scorching, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat called "epiglottis" be cut off; and one should not help by this method, because all the veins and the phlegm of the patient are hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two almonds.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the disease is in the channel of phlegm, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid death from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we must cut it below III or IV small transverse slits, between II circles or according to the size of the sinus, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is fearful, then he must extend the skin of the throat to the chin, then cut open the heart until it reaches the jawbone; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then cut off the liver as we have said; and it is proven by the section of the phlegm from the jaw that jumps with force through the broken place, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the hour has passed during which strangulation is feared, join together the two lips of the heart's wound, and stitch it all up without bandages; then administer medicines that promote the growth of flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasim says that this should not be done until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and lacks breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Therefore, the epiglottis is cut so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and for this reason the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the mischief of the disease has passed, which passes in three or four days. And then they commanded to close the wound and cure it until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young woman took a knife and stabbed herself in the throat, cutting part of the cartilage of the larynx; and I was called to treat her, and found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had come out of it, and although it had not struck a vein or a main artery except for the throat, and the wind was coming out strongly through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing more happened to the maiden except that she became hoarse of voice, and afterwards returned to her usual state; therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 These abscesses are called "throat hernias," and they are large abscesses of the color of jet, and they occur often in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; in the natural type there is no pus.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accident is in two ways, one of which resembles a boil to us, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from our vein; and there is fear, and it is not right to work on making a hole except in that which is small, and test and check all around: if you find it like I know a boil, and it does not touch any vein, then cut it, as one cuts the nose, and draw out all its hair, if there is any; and investigate well quickly, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 There are many kinds of us, all of which I will describe the resemblances; and now it is necessary for me to say all the differences that exist between our (thing) and issuing (from a thing).
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 I say that the issue occurs during fever and while holding heat until the inflammation has passed and putrefaction is complete; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 With the new issue, there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains pus, which is its own sac and corresponds to the body's color, beginning like a pustule and growing large; and they are of two kinds, either greasy or moist, and many colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 It is necessary that when you come to the care of the pustule, you first prove and inquire with all the instrument called "entromissoire," according to what its form will be in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you take the moistest place you find on the abscess, and turn your two fingers little by little, so that you know that the instrument has reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intromitter, and be careful that it does not jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If the running moisture, what color it has, then cut into it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the intromitter comes more moisture, know that it is greasy, so then cut it in a cross shape, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape from each side and keep the skin where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the knot; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 Car if anything remains, the nose returns many times; and if a piece remains and the blood irritates, fill the wound with some corrosive, burning powders, constrict the wound, and place soothing things on the hot abscess, and treat with other treatments until healed; and if the nose is large, then stitch the two lips of the wound, and treat those who have flesh torn.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 and if the vein swells against you or otherwise, then hurry and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound becomes gangrenous, and the blood's boiling calms; then return to treat whatever remains of the vein.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Vez ci = Here are the shapes of the inserted instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small. And there are three squares that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they too are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistula. And they are like the needles with which one sews the sorceries, and they are made of brass, or iron, or silver; and those that are yellow in color are most valuable, and they are more proven for black pitch to encircle the fistulas' carbuncles. And they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of the onions are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are onions that have two curves of three types; and there are onions that have three curves, and they are also of three types; and there are onions that have two curves, and onions with only one curve, and they are also of three types; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these which one makes are sharp, and there are some that cut only from one side, with which one scrapes the nails so that one does not cut the vein or the nerve; and among these instruments are the curved scissors held in sheaths, so that the patient is unaware of them when opening abscesses; and they come in three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a lancet, according to this form, with which one lets blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And one places it sometimes in a place that heals promptly the veins, and the arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to be corrupted, to the point that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must follow this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 then peel off the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that encourages flesh growth, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and continue the treatment until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size as happens in women, then make two incisions above the two similar folds; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.; then peel off the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and administer as we have said in sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely done, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remainder and the fat, then continue the treatment until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 of the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 These abscesses that occur under the armpits are hard and resemble scrofulas, which may contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus in the abscess has been emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat it with suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then cut it as we have said for cutting scrofula, and if pus comes out of the wound, apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is torn, and the skin that is above it is swollen, there often follow abscesses, and the same happens with an inflamed vein and abscess; and one knows this when it is due to the artery, for then the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you sense a constriction; and when it is due to the vein, reason is lacking in appearance; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the nails and at the angles and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
