It is therefore necessary to avoid the iron cure, and that which is on the head should be avoided as well; and in the case of artery swelling, make an incision above the skin lengthwise; then work the cut along the edges, and neatly separate the artery from the veins, so that it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath it, and make it pierce through to the other side, and constrict the artery with double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries which are in the temples; then bind the place between the two ligatures with a tourniquet so that the blood issuing from there is released, and let the abscess be relieved; then apply the cure that is common to all, until the ligature falls off; then treat it with ointments appropriate to this, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to the cutting of the vein, you should stain your hand with what you can from the abscess over all the skin, then insert the needle under the place that you are holding in your hand, and make it pierce through, and let there be a double thread so that you draw it out on the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, with one end of the thread to two knots at two ends of the thread; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then insert another needle all along the one thread underneath all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and constrict the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the superfluousness comes out, then cut the superfluity of the skin and leave that which is bound; then put a cloth moistened in wine and oil on top, then apply dressings and ointments appropriate to this until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	 of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Similarly, as abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, so they also come in the nerves when they are struck or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color resembles that of the flesh, and it has many dispositions without pain; and when it is pressed strongly, then the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the flesh, but below the skin; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor downwards or upwards, and that which is in the joints must not be cut with iron: lest contraction may occur; and that which is in the head or forehead, pierce the skin with a needle.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut it at its root; if it is large, suspend it with a hook, scrape it, then remove it and close the wound with stitches, and treat until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging large abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in the stomach and not in any other place, and it is an illness called "fungus" due to its similarity to them; and the root is subtle, and the head large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his stomach which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were always wet.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I sliced them and found that one weighed XVIII ounces, and the other VI З., and the work in the incision is such that you should check if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist and of subtle root; then cut with a wide spatula, and have the cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the wound overwhelms you, then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made linen thread, and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not stop pulling the linen thread until it cuts the artery, and each time without difficulty; and if the roots are large, fear also to cut immediately because of the belly, but you can cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and be careful not to cut the vein which is of dark color and poor appearance and milky look.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Car this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of crusts later.
quant li boude ist fuer	 When the boil is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the boil comes from the cauterization of a wound or rupture in the intestines, and it is on the abdomen and there are some boils as happens in other ruptures, either from bleeding of veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from flatulence; and if it is due to rupture of the intestine and exits through the anus, then the color of the abscess resembles that of the body, and it is a minor thing without pain, and exits in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses on both sides it returns, and then comes back, and perhaps it becomes narrowed, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and through great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and it appears well when you press it in your hand, not constraining at all; and if it is due to blood, the abscess appears large and hard, and it is fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to touch, and the work is such that you should examine whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 You must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bladder, you must command the patient to hold his leg, and be stretched out straight; then sign around all over the belly; then order him to lie quietly between your hands; then go around the place that you have signed with all the spatula; then extend half of the abscess on top of all the great uncine; then bind it around with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot of the bond be tight; then work half of the abscess extended on the ligature, and put your index finger in it, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught in the ligature, unfasten it, and push the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the bladder, take it with the uncine, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery or vein causes resistance, go around well, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two strong threads through them, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you make perforate; then press the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it rots, and let the dead flesh rot by itself; or cut it when it is softened and rotten, then cure the abscess as it should be cured, and close the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it should be cured, and suture the place.
dou chancre	 of cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have said in the division the likenesses of cancer, and how one should work there with medicines, and how one must avoid the cure of iron; and we say that cancer infects the flesh, and great care is needed in the cure, and the ancients said that when the cancer is in a place where it can be scraped off, such as cancer which is on breasts, and on thighs, and similar places, one must scrape off all of it when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, then one should not approach it, for I have never seen anyone heal from it; nor has anyone ever healed from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile; then make him fast if he has a manifest repletion, then take the patient to a good place to perform the work; then throw your nails into the cancer, and the hair from all sides, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press well on the area with your hand or with something else, and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the blood is blackened; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	 Of diabetes
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 And we have said in the division the resemblances of diabetes, and in what manner the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each resemblance, and the cure that is done by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: this one is only drained; and one should not touch with iron in these two resemblances: that is to know, tympanites and hydrops, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this resemblance of diabetes which is called "dropsy" by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides diabetes, such as dropsy and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease but diabetes alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the assistant presses the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the pointed spatula in this manner:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And it should cut through two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 And the point should not be so deep that it can reach the intestines when inserted and not injure them; then look to see if the dropsy is towards the intestines: in this case, you must make an incision above the navel, three fingers' width below the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, your incision should be on the left side of the navel; and if it is due to bladder problems, it should be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the superfluous fluids do not run to this weak spot; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, remove it, and lift your hand to all the tissue between the skin and the membrane as if scraping to the quantity of a fingernail or thereabouts; then pierce the membrane until the tissue comes to the desired place, which is the place of the water, then draw strongly, and pour into this instrument whose shape is thus:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and it is of light brass or iron, and in the lower part there is a small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which the scribes cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 At the top is the air hole, so that when the instrument comes to water, then it immediately rises on the instrument; empty now half or a third, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, perhaps the patient will die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then remove the instrument and retain the water, and it is now retained by the cork that stops the hole that is on the syringe, which I have mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then the instrument begins again the next day, if you see the patient suffering this way, and draw a small quantity of water; do this every day, and be careful not to hurry until there remains only a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient and leave much water in him, cure him with a grave or hot sand, and greatly by sweating, bathing, and sun exposure, and dye him with wine; and cure him with desiccative medicines until he is dried out, and cauterize on the stomach, liver, and spleen after removing the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 of the blockage of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 It happens sometimes that children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Then it should be pierced immediately with a very fine needle according to this manner:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then put in the hole a small plug of pine, and tie it and hold it thus for III days or IV and when he wishes to make urine, let the plug be removed, and make urine, and then replace it; and perhaps it is not necessary, because the urine that comes out will not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 If the hole is small, let him be treated with the pine plug, as we have said, so that it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the hole in its proper place are injured, for some are born with the hole at the tip of the penis, so that they cannot urinate forward unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the glans, and this is a serious disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the manner of the work is such that the patient often lies on his back, then extend the head of the verge and the cup as wide as a feather's shaft, so that the hole reaches in the middle, as it should; and beware of bleeding that often occurs there, and if it does happen, staunch it with whatever staunches blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 of the pustules of the verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Often these albathes come in the verge, and it is an ugly appearance of foul flesh; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; therefore you must take them at the first subtle sign, and cut and clean all of them, then apply a moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment; then heal with diligent ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the leprosy is malignant, of foul color and stench, then you must apply cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it off, and if the leprosy is in part within the flesh and in part outside of it, then you must first remove the leprosy that is inside; and when it is healed, then treat the one that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you treat them together, it is not certain that the head of the flesh will not be perforated, and blackness and corruption come into its flesh and the joint; thus one must cut away everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a poultice of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and beans, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if blood is flowing out, then use the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery helps in two situations together: that is to say, for the flow of blood, and for decay; and if the head of the penis is decayed and retracts, then you must insert into the duct of the penis a cane made of lead, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair at the tip of the penis happens to those who have not been circumcised, if it occurs due to injury or abscess, then you should scrape it with a heated instrument until the foreskin is freed, and the head of the penis is delivered from all sides; and if it is difficult to discuss this, then you should scrape with a spatula some at the tip of the penis and the skin; then gently cut between two, and put there a fine cloth of linen moistened in cold water, so that it does not adhere again.
de la circoncision	 Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not the separation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this task by our own will and properly on children, it is necessary to do the best work and the lightest for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children because they do not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have gained through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen the greatest part of masters and surgeons performing circumcision on Dal, at forces, and on the whole novacula; thus the heart was pierced because there are two membranes, and by chance one cuts the upper one and the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 Or the patient recovers quickly, and the pain is doubled; at the mundification from the nail, the point of the member is not secure; and at the mundification of the fingernail, sometimes the iron slips away, ruining the work, and often it turns out that no mundification was needed, which I have experienced.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 From the mundification done with forceps on all the parts of the limb, I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forceps cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Because when you press your hand and cut equally in all directions as long as you hold the limb; but let the thread be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child, if it understands, think that you are only tying the thread around the member, and then make him happy in every way you can; then hold it straight between your hands, and return the forceps between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them or any of the instruments; then press your hand to the member and blow into the heart, and draw it up until the head of the member is inside; then clean it well of the dirt that has gathered there, then bind the place tightly with a double thread, then bind it below one finger to another ligature; and hold it by two fingers of the second finger above the little finger and the index finger, and cut between the two ligatures, then lift the heart quickly and draw out the head of the member; then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is the cure; and put powder on it and on top of the powder a piece of cloth soaked in egg white tempered with rose water, confected with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The heads should be sharp and cutting, and the heads should also be as large as the fingers equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The error in mundification is when the core inside follows the incision; therefore, you must stretch it to your fingernail before the place forms an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with pincers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if it goes on for three days, and what is under the skin is swollen, leave it until that abscess is appeased, and lightly scratch off the scab; then cut as you can move, and be careful of the part of the skin, so that it will not harm it at all.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure then the place of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatment of powders, and if the heart is cut excessively and it goes above, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 of the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is caused by the formation of stones, or congealed blood, or a boil, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is located in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the upper part of the back, and have the patient restrain his breath as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constricted to force out the stone above, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which here is the form: and let it be made of fine silver, lightly drawn, like the feather of a bird; and let its tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the issue of the urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie at the end a bag of wool or cotton, and insert the end of the thread into the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it until the end of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair, and wash the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, as far as it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward until the bladder, and the patient will feel it coming up to the empty space, and this is not done unless the passage through which it goes is twisted; then draw the thread all with the wool bag little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and let the urine flow; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When there are scrapes or blood in the bladder, or rotting has gathered there, and you wish to instill water and medicines, you must first make everything with an instrument called "clepsedre," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see. And let the place through which the medicine passes be such that it stops up the tube well without addition, so that it can draw out the moisture and push when necessary; and when you wish to pour your medicines into the bladder, put the head of the enema into the moisture, and pull on the puller that is inside. Thus, you will draw the moisture into the enema bag, then strongly reinsert the puller; thus, the moisture will enter, and will now come to the bladder so that the patient will feel it; this is the form of the subtle enema with which one enemaizes the bladder: here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below it falls to the chest or the liver; then take a sheep's bladder and put in the moisture with which you wish to enema the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts tightly with a double good thread, and heat the pouch of that moisture over the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the pipe, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture has entered, so that the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as one would assemble a bucket, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have already said in the division the types of stones, and the extraction with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in which stone one should work on cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is in the bladder happens more often to children, and it is a sign that there is water from the bladder like water in its subtlety; and there is urine, and it causes the patient's penis to swell, and he urinates frequently, and then he becomes constipated; and at many of these urinations the base is found; and the healing of children is light until they are four years old, and it is very severe in the elderly, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes hinders in searching for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and lift and move them downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes comes out from above; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is fully inclined downwards; then seek it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten now to cut into the stone.  ()
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall at the touch of all, moisten your finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adolescent; and push it into its base, and look for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, guide it to the neck of the bladder; then press on top of your finger, and expel it outside where you want to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand over the testicles upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the part where the cut is made; then insert the spatula carefully, of which this is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And make between those who are between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the vein; and let it be straight upon the stone, and your two fingers should always be on the anus, and let the cut across be such that it is wide on the outside, and narrow within, according to the size of the stone, not too large. By chance, the pressure of the finger in the anus makes it come out without effort; and know that there are some stones with angles and edges: they are difficult to remove; and there are some which are below, similar to a glass bead, and round, from which removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 To those with angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, then you must apply tongs that are like a file at the end, to squeeze the stone so that it does not escape. Or you insert beneath a subtle instrument curved at the end; and if you cannot trick it this way, widen the pouch where the opening is, and if the urine flows out, then constrict it with vitriol. And if there are more than one stone, first push the largest into the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then draw it out, and afterwards the smaller ones, if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then it must be cauterized, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine continually flows from there so that the wound cannot close; nevertheless, strive to pull it out, or break it with pincers in pieces; and when you have completed your work, then fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put on top a moistened cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the hot abscess; then let the patient rest on his back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you dislocate it, wash very well the place with oil and water, then treat it with a delicate ointment and a basil ointment, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if this abscess comes into the wound and there are corrosions, and congelations of blood in the bladder, and the urine is retained because it goes out with the urine: then stick your finger in the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and the skin; then wash the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help it in all ways you know until it is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat it, you bind the two thighs together and apply the medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the urethra, and stuck, and urine cannot come out; so the treatment of this that I say is, that you cut it many times, and one is freed from the cutting by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven this thus.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take an iron tool according to this shape and it should be at three corners fixed in one stake:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then take a thread and tie it around the rod under the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then push the iron tool into the rod lightly, until it reaches the stone; and turn the iron tool in your hand against the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come out soon, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken quickly and forced out with the urine, then the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for some reason that prevents it, tie a thread underneath the stone and another on top, then insert the rod towards the stone between the two threads, then force it out, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood that is in the wound; and continue the treatment until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	 of the female bladder stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It rarely happens that a woman has a bladder stone, and when it does occur, the treatment is difficult and is hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who will reveal herself to the physicians, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is such that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-versed in this hand art; and the fourth manner is such that the stone of the woman is more embedded than the stone of the man, for which reason it requires a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity demands this, then you must take a midwife well-versed in this, and one scarcely finds her, and if you do not find her, then seek a subtle male doctor; and present him with a wise old woman who is experienced in women's lives, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command that she perform what you instruct concerning the search for the stone; and take great care to see if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the fundament and seek the stone; and if she finds it, she should constrain it under her finger, and recommend that she insert her finger into the vulva of the patient, and seek and press her left hand strongly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, then she must move it from side to side from the entry of the bladder downwards until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the con, where it is more suited, and press on the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the first cut be small; then push the reed into the cut, if you feel the stone so tightly clamp the wound until the stone can come out with force.

Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood overcomes you, place vitriol plaster on the spot, and hold it there for an hour until the blood is stanched; then return to your work until the stone is weakened, and have the instruments that I told you about for the extraction of the stone in men to help you in your work; and if the blood overcomes you, and it is from the artery that is cut, place the powder on the spot and bandage with cloths and bandages, and do not attempt this again, and leave the stone alone, do not pull it out, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood is soothed, and the place is numb, return to your work until the stone is weakened.
de hernie carnouse	 Of flesh-based hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 Aquatic hernia is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white sack that is below the heart of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "sack," and sometimes it is properly in the cloth of the egg, so one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white sack that we have said; and these do not happen unless there are pockets.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the origin of this hernia is from weakness in the testicles, and that substance is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it comes from a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: it is either yellowish, or without red, or black, or white like water, and this happens often; and these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is in the white sack that we have mentioned, then the abscess is reasonable, a long pocket like the shape of an egg, and the testicle does not open, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, the abscess is round with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the leather of the thighs and the white flesh, one feels it well; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine all the affected area thoroughly, from which the form comes before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what follows the affected area, judge what is inside it.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with fire, the patient must be seated according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then have him sit on his back, on something not too high, and place many cloths underneath him; then have him sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on his right, and extend the iron rod along one of the two ribs of the curve of the thighs; then take the spatula knife, and cut the skin of the thighs in a straight line from top to bottom until near the groin, and let your cut be entirely straight while dividing the skin of the thighs up to the white flesh, and carefully peel it according to your ability; then puncture the white flesh completely with water through a large hole, and extract all the water, and then apply your fingers, and stretch the white flesh upward; and do not touch the curve of the thighs, but only the white flesh; cut the side of him entirely or in pieces as well, so that if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return; and if the egg jumps out of your work, bring it back into its place when you have completed the work on the white flesh; then sew the two lips of the curve of the thighs with a stitch, then cure him as the other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you bind the vessels that are suspended, suspecting the flow of blood; then cut the coccyx throughout the suspension, and extract the egg, and heal it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if the vein is divided into two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe away the blood, and put in the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and put on top of the two coccyxes another linen moistened in wine and oil, and put over them double-layered cloths, and bind it all up with a bandage that follows this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths, and fill them with wool according to this pattern and sew them together in the collar of the breeches, and let one of the heads take from the foundation up to the back, and the other at the wrist; and the other two heads on the two ankles, and let all the tightening be in the loop of the breeches; and sometimes this wrap for cautery is used instead of an iron tailoring knife, and it is that you take a subtle surgical knife, and cut the skin of the testicles, and heat it as we have said, so that the white part that contains the water is exposed; then take the cautery in this form, and pierce that white part at the corners, and scrape with this hot subtle cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cut in all the ways that you can, until you excise everything; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and beware of bleeding or wounds caused by the tailoring work; and if anything goes against you, whether it is an abscess or bleeding or something else, then cure what goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this work because of its horror, then use perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are certain through the indications that we have said that there is aquous humor there, then make the patient sit on a high seat; pierce the abscess in the lower part as wide as possible, and place the perforation along the length of the body; and let the opening be large so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the spot, and bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining water, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument with which one draws water from dropsical patients, whose form has been described above; and enlarge the opening of the wound, and know that the water will return, and it will collect again after six months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as before, and thus the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the cutting of this vein there is fear in many conditions, which is why it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you the workings and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 I say therefore that many abscesses come in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this is in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 This is to say by superfluous acid and acute, which spreads to the testicles, or from blows; and the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and it finds no pain, and the abscess is grave; and sometimes an abscess is called dangerous and painful, and of a red color, and sometimes comes from a swollen vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is due to narrowing of an artery, it is known by the hot condition of an abscess, when you press it against your fingers; and you must not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 That which is done with inflammation of a vein is known by its condition at the expression from the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the cut on this likeness, and on other wounds; and it is that you cut the heart of the coions, then let the egg rise up, and draw out the white thoroughly, and deliver the membrane from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already hardened with these wounds, then it is necessary that you draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is full of pus or in those which are inside the vessels, then it is necessary that you deliver all that matter, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the birthplace of the flesh is at the back, then you must cut all of it and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess enveloped in a covering similar to a bud, with the softening of the testicles, and if the patient moves greatly when he walks; and the treatment of this disease is almost as dangerous as the previous one, nevertheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the scrotal suspension down to your thighs, to all the vessels close to the penis, and hold them firmly; then cut with a sharp scalpel across the vessels until they are exposed, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein has come out, and tie again at the other end; then cut them straight in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt humors; then treat the wound as the others where the bone is injured, so that no vessel bursts that nourishes one of the testicles; for by this there is no harm, and if all the vessels become visible, it is necessary to pull the testicles to all the vessels; so that the flesh does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry out and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	 of the suturing of the sinus
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The occurrences of this hernia are from the section that comes to the sinus, or the extension on the belly in the area of the groin, because the intestines descend from that suture to one of the testicles; and this suture is either in the sinus, or in the extension of it, and these two types come from many causes: from a blow, or from a jump, or from a belch, or from lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the sign when it is from the extension of the sinus is that it comes little by little, over a long time, and does not happen suddenly; and the abscess is equal to the depth, because the sinus presses against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is that when it is from the section of the synaxis, it causes sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess appears diverse, under the skin nearby, and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body lacking the synaxis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the circles go with the intestine, and they are retained within, causing the patient to suffer great pain, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these treatments by iron, for fear of which it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the method of treatment is such that you instruct the patient to pull out the intestine with his hand into the wound, if he can reach it; then let him be bound around his neck, between your hands, and lift the thighs; then place the heart above, and cut all the skin from the testicles lengthwise; then insert the liver of the groin inside accordingly as needed to open the wound, so that the eggs may come out; then peel off the synaxis which is under the skin of the testicles, until the hard white synaxis is uncovered on all sides; then insert your index finger in that which follows the testicle, into what is between the white synaxis which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second synaxis, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second synaxis; and then move to the right hand inside the heart of the testicles, and raise the white synaxis up to your left hand, and lift the egg with all the synaxis towards the groin; and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and release that which is tied behind the ligament; and check with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped around the hard white synaxis, and if you find anything, push it down into the belly below; then take a needle with a thread of one hundred threads made from ten threads, and insert it in the back part of the synaxis which is after the skin of the testicles, behind the groin, then cut the knots that appear from the threads until there are four threads;
