then gather them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the synaxis which we have said is under the skin of the testicles with a strong thread of two parts; then wrap the knots of the threads and tie them firmly with two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them may enter into it, so that an abscess does not form there; and place the ligature again according to the first long ligature, two fingers from that one, and after these two ligatures leave the synaxis which is under the heart of the testicles the width of a finger; and then cut in the part which is under the skin of the testicles until the blood runs, as we have said before; then apply wool moistened with oil to the wounds, and place the ligature which we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	 And sometimes we cauterize the white tissue that we have mentioned after the incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this happens often, and let the pus drain by itself; and if it delays in draining, then apply hot water and place on it what we have said, until it drains; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this case, I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done in the same way as the vessel which is with the bladder, in such a manner that you tie the vessels after cutting them lightly below; then cut through the middle, and treat the abscess with what we have mentioned, until the vessels drain; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 When the bowels burst into the anus, as we have said, and open the place; and let none of the intestines protrude into the scrotum, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; and nevertheless, if it stays too long in this state, the wound or hernia will grow until the intestines protrude; and this happens because of the extension of the hernia that is in the anus, as we have said, for it is extended, then the place is softened and swollen and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; and sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and let the patient lie on his back between your hands, then cut the inflamed place of the hernia wide according to the width of three fingers; and then extract the hernia that is under the skin like the previous, then take the needle and put it on the visible part of the hernia; and press deeply into the belly, then sew the two visible parts of the hernia onto the head of the needle, and sew one and the other; then extract the head of the needle, and do not cut the hernia or extend the egg or anything else, as I have made you know in the cure of the intestinal entrapment; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, clean and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The suture is constricting and has no appearance in the stitching, and the cautery is better in this place and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Many times the skin of the testicles is softened in some men, because the parts that are inside are softened and it can be seen; and it is necessary that when one wants to heal it, that the patient lies on his back, and cut the softened skin onto the natural skin; then join the two lips with a stitch, and if you wish, sew first the superfluous part of the softened skin with three or four strong stitches; then cut between the stitches, and heal it as the other wounds until it is healed, and let the threads fall.
dou chastrement	 of the cautery
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that cauterization is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the physician knows how to answer when asked about it, and knows the treatment; and the other reason is that we often need to use cauterization on some animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and dogs and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that cauterization is done in two ways: by attraction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the one that we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the skin is softened and loose; then take it with your hand, until it is replaced and you no longer feel it.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Of castration of the male: you must hold the animal, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie the cord, and cut above each testicle one time, when you have well skinned them; and leave some of the fat and the fine fat that is on the vessels; and this manner of castration is better than that done by attraction, because at attraction there may remain accidentally something from the testicles, which causes the animal to desire lust; then heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	 Of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 Hermaphroditism occurs in men in two ways: one is that between the two testicles there appears as if by the nature of a woman, where there is hair, and sometimes urine flows from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And another manner is for women, and it is placed on the wrist like a rod and two ounces.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for both men and women is that you should cut the cartilages together, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine flows through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	 of the temples
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Tentigene is a cartilage on the natural part, so that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you cut off the superfluity of the tentigene with your hand or scissors, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that blood does not come out, then treat it with another treatment until it heals; and for another cartilage that grows at the mouth of the womb, and fills up, and perhaps protrudes, and is like a cow's udder, and therefore the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it is necessary for you to cut it, as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it is healed.
de erratique	 erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic is when the woman's nature is not understood, or the opening is small; and it can be natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come upon it; whether it is caused by a narrowing of the hips, or by subtle or thick sperm, and it forms deep in the womb, or on the sides, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation; and knowledge of this condition comes from examining the vagina.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the protrusion is apparent near, seek two fingers or a thread.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 If the subtle symphysis is near the II livres, hasten and do thus: place your II fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, with her legs spread; then extend the II livres very strongly, so that the subtle symphysis is open, and there is swelling; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and let the woman lie down each day, so that it may not heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the symphysis is hard and thick, then you should cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the swelling is of flesh born, then suspend it with an onion and cut it; and have the blood-stanching medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, abundant in egg white; then apply a wide piece of lead, so that the wound may not heal; and thus for a long time, and let him use a linen tent; then he should be treated with other treatments until he is healthy.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when a wound occurs on the head, it should be covered in this manner, unless it is an abscess that has broken open.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For the burst abscess that is on the head, one should not touch or do anything with fire.
des emorroides	 of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are usually without skin, and when hemorrhoids are old, they turn black; and we have already said in the division their similarities, and their signs, and I will say here those that can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and blackening, when they are completely protruding from the head and do not protrude to touch, then there is no treatment by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Ceux qui sont à l'entrée de la plaie, que l'on peut sentir, sont ceux que l'on peut traiter.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Those who are at the edge of the wound, which can be felt, are those that can be treated.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it stops bleeding, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not stop, have cupping glasses applied to the back and breasts without cutting; then take wool, soak it in plantain juice or hawthorn juice with old wine, and apply to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess is quiet, then cauterize the place of the swelling until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a sharp head, so you should cover it as I have said above; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	 of the pustules of the face
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscesses come to the face, such as cancer and piercing abscesses and herpes and styes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is therefore necessary that I speak in this treatise about the hot abscess that comes to the face, which is not one of the abscesses that swell quickly; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the wound dry until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and place two small chairs where he can lean back, and support his back and bring his feet together at the outer side of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then succor give him towards the left side, and bring the instrument used to work the opening of the wound, from which later comes the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument being brought, that you first insert a needle to know the depth of the wound, so that what enters into the instrument does not go in deeper than it should, and that it does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is too large, then cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he put the horn of the instrument on top, and that he hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and one makes an incision with a soft hand, it must be covered at the top with a layer of leek spathe; and when the wound is emptied, it should be placed in the wound moist cloths in rose oil or in dry green oil; and place the cloth outside the wound on the edge of the flesh, and place on top of the flesh and on the arm a clean cloth moistened in water where the mallows are cooked; then cure after two days of ointment fitting to that, as long as it is healed; and sometimes lift the flesh and the wound with an enema of water and honey, and then of water with roots of lily and aristolochia long be cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 Et s'il y a une blessure dans la chair, il faut éviter d'utiliser le fer pour la cautériser, mais traite-la comme nous l'avons décrit dans la section sur les divisions.
de l’enfantement	 du accouchement
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 Quant li fous enfans veut issir par la baise, cil n’a pas en lui la figure de l’enfantement naturel; car il vient mal a point, et est tout contrarie a son naturel. Et tu ne le deves mie aidier fors s’il te requiert, car se il ne te requiert mie, si n’est pas bien fait.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Because it sometimes happens to his feet, and comes upon the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, or his back, and is turned by chance onto his neck, and in other bad shapes; thus, it is necessary for the nurse that she be wise and skillful in these things, and guard against error and deceit, and I will show you all the figures how one should help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes upon his head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her virtue is weak, then let her sit on a saddle, where women hold her; and arise her nature with oil or cooked fenugreek, and then the nurse puts between his teeth the little spatula whose form is this:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And cut the secondine, and slice towards its nail until the moisture inside flows out; and hold the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to give the woman a clister (enema) of fenugreek powder with sesame oil; then make her drink and cough up condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out strongly, then you must gently push them back a little at a time; and if they cannot go in, put the woman on a chair and raise her feet high; then tilt the chair to the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall when it is tilted; and if the hands cannot go in and the child dies, cut off the hands with the knife mentioned earlier, and extract the child, and treat them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's exit onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes onto its feet, it is necessary to push upwards; and then turn it a little at a time until it is straight; then take it by one of its feet and extend it a little at a time.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 When he jumps up to his knees, command him to cough and let him sneeze as needed; if he jumps further, so be it with God’s will.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if he does not jump further as we have said, then turn him a little at a time until he is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	 For then he will have gone lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not come forth as we have said, then take mullein of altitude, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all together in a mortar; and put this ointment on the woman’s nature inside and outside; then make her sit in hot water up to the ribs; and when she is well moistened below, give her a drink of honey wine, and place it under her, and leave her for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for now the child will jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	 from the child’s exit onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, let the midwife place her hands little by little; then she should be lifted onto his neck, and his feet should hang down, and he should lie on the bed; and bend his hands little by little, and then take his hands above the belly, and remove the pillows from below, until it is prepared to descend; and if the child does not jump, take his feet and move them very well, then move the belly up, then put your hands there; and draw the child little by little; and command the woman to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	 of the child's exit that comes from the side a hand's width wide
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to maneuver to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, then make the woman rise and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie down on a bed, and spread her legs widely; then introduce the instrument that I have described; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then study to bring back the hand; and take the child according to its natural shape, and make it sneeze, and command that she grasp herself until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	 of the exit of the child onto its neck, and let its hands be spread, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the midwife take her hand, then turn it little by little, and gently lift it; and when it is equal, put on the natural instrument of height and oil, as we have said, then command that she move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and command that she grasp herself; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	 of this same manner to all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it happens in this manner to all the second part, then cut the second part with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child presses on its face and on its neck, then cut from the base so that it is not retained, and kill the child; then push the child back inside, as much as you need to place it, and instruct the woman to hold herself some time: then it will come out lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	 of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	 Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two is a strange thing, and they do not live, except rarely; I know that they are multiplied by the sperm that separates them, which is tied to the base; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out violently, then treat it as we have said, and let the wound be subtle, and make it quickly and lightly, just as she does; and do so that he may move to safety.
de plusors enfans	 of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or many up to XV, and all are perfectly formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the wound know all these things, for perhaps similar things happen; thus do as is proper.
de l’enfant mort	 of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for the dead child in the womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound constitution, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should be placed on her back, and her head inclined downward, and her legs raised; and the assistant holds the two parts, where she lies in the bed so that she is not drawn down by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the womb with moist oils with a mixture of althea and fenugreek and flaxseed, then anoint your hands with these oils and these mixtures; then gently insert them into the womb, then find one place where she can insert the needles so that they are suitable for this purpose, and take care if the child is well-prepared that it should descend onto its head; then fix the needles in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palate or under his beard or in his forehead or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then fix it in the heel and in the middle of the ribs; and it is necessary that you hold the needle with your right hand, and place the hook between your fingers of the left hand, and gently insert all your hand, and fix the needle in any of these places that we have said, until you come to the empty space; and this is the shape of the needle:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then insert against the other bone, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then move them equally in one direction and another to make it come out, and let the bones be notched to hold it, as shown here.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, then anoint the bail with some of his fingers in oil, and push it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if nothing remains, place this bone higher up, and do this until it all comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to constriction, it is necessary that you wrap it on a cloth until it all comes out; then cut off at the joint of the foot or at the heel, and so must you do with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is narrow in the birth canal, or if there is a sharp angle at the crown of the head, then you must insert the sharp spatula between your fingers, and split the crown and extract the sharp angle; or use the instrument called "almidach," by which the form comes with the instruments mentioned in the chapter following this one. And do the same if the child has a large head naturally. Then draw out the bones with forceps, and if the head protrudes and is stuck in the birth canal, then it should be cut open until the moisture within the bladder is released; and if it cannot come out, then strike it into pieces with as much force as you can; and if the belly or under the ribs are swollen, then you must pierce them until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	 And if the child is on its feet, then the attraction is light, and the adjustment to the mother's mouth is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is extended at the stomach or the chest, then you must stretch it on a cloth wrapped around your hand; and open the stomach or the chest until the moisture inside is corrected; and if other members are removed and the head remains, then insert your hand into the deepest part of the womb, and pull it up to the mouth of the womb; then put one or two onions in, and pull strongly; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to a hot abscess that has formed there, then do not work at it, but rather apply moist and fatty things; and administer poultices, and cook them in softening and moisturizing water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the child is on its side, and you can place it flat, then proceed as we have said with the living child; but if you cannot, then draw out the foetus piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 And when you have done this, proceed as we have said in the case of abscesses that come to married women; and if there is bleeding, place her in warm water to restrain it, and administer other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	 And I saw a woman whose womb held a dead child, then another grew above it, and the other died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	 After a long time, an abscess formed in her belly, and swelled until it burst, and began to fester greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	 I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but the wound could not be healed.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	 I applied a strong drawing plaster, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	 I was greatly astonished by this, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	 So I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I cleaned the wound, and removed many bones until the woman was in better condition; and she lived for a long time thus, and always exuded a little pus from that place; and I have remembered this chapter only because when the master finds something strange, he should know how to apply help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	 To bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	 Here comes the form of the press, which is used for the books; and at two turns are the two heads of the two levers.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 However, let the horns be more subtle than the press, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the wood be two fingers wide, and the edge of the tree one finger, and in length a palm and a half; and between the two levers there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are fitted in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two adjustments are placed at the mouth of the bone to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 A different form, more subtle and lighter, be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the likeness of tongs; and have at the two ends two adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the vulva with all the instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, feet dangling and legs spread, then push the two adjustments together into the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand along the entire instrument, as you have done with the tongs equally, according to the quantity that you wish to open the mouth of the vulva, until the old woman does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	 This instrument is all sharpened, and their appearances are diverse; and when the physician has prepared them, the work is faster, and higher for men due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	 Do not despise the instrument before it has been prepared, because their needs are not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the placenta is retained after childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze forcefully, and press your hands against her mouth and nose; if she expels it in this way, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, then take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cinnamon, and centaury; all these herbs or some of them are cooked in water over the fire; then put a tube from the pot into the hole in the lid, and the other end in the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the steam enters the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	 If the second skin (blister) bursts quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment and is not broken, then instruct the patient to moisten their left hand in linseed oil or mustard plaster of lupine, then apply it to the blister, and search for the second skin; and when she finds it, she should take hold of it and stretch it little by little evenly, so that the flesh does not tear during removal; but it must be moved gently to the right and left, and then pull; thus it will come out and drain.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the flesh is narrowly constricted, we have spoken of treatment by sneezing and herb fumigation; and if it does not burst from all that has been said, be careful not to rush when pulling; but you must tie what is at the mouth of the flesh to the thigh of the woman, then administer an enema with four-compound oil; thus it will putrefy and soften, and come out; however, when it putrefies, it brings a bad odor to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	 If therefore, it is necessary to use suitable fumigations for this purpose: some of the ancients have proven fumigations with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	 The form of the instrument used to fumigate the woman for retaining the flowers and the second stage is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 It is made of glass, similar to a reed, and the fine end is placed in the vagina, while the wider end rests on the fire; and let the fumigation be on hot coals, and continue until it has thoroughly dried out, then begin again with another.
de percier lou fondement	 to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born whose anus is not pierced, but rather closed by a thin membrane: it is therefore necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger, and not with a sharp spatula; and she should be careful that she does not touch the child’s genitals. Then she should place a cloth moistened in wine and oil over it, and continue the care of ointment until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	 And if you doubt that it will not heal, then put a lead weight through the hole, and leave it for fewer days, and remove it when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	 And sometimes this obstruction comes from a sudden wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cover that suddenness: and if it is healed, as we have said with the lead weight.
de la fistule dou fondement	 of the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from beneath the anus are nodules, and those that come near the anus from below or in the space of the two parts, whether one fistula or several; and when this nodule is old, it works, and it brings with it more moisture, either white or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by this, that there comes out from them during excretion or wind, and sometimes one bursts.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	 And so for fissures that penetrate to the bladder, and halfway through the penis; and they reach to the groin, and even to the testicles.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one knows if the fissure penetrates the anus or not: and it is that you insert your finger into the anus, and push a fine needle of iron or steel into the fissure when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is curvature, then you push a fine lead tent or a horse hair into it until you feel the tent or the hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and nothing comes out of the opening—neither excrement nor gas nor pus—as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	 And when the fistula reaches to the bladder or to the channel of urine, then the urine leaks out and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated to the hip joint, then the tendon comes to that place; if there is no tortuosity and the pain is around the wound, then it leaks out constantly, and neither medicine nor cauterization by ointment helps; and in these perforating fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and foolish doctors waste their time on them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one that is not perforating and is not ancient, there is hope for healing by iron, as I have experienced; and it is that the patient lies on his back between your hands; and you raise his legs up to his hips, and let his hips be inclined towards his belly; then insert a tendon of brass, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the tendon comes out.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 Se the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger inside, if you feel that the tent has been pierced; and if it is discovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then know that it is perforated; so do not work on it as one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 It is said, however, that one can heal some well, but this happens rarely; and the help that one provides, it is that one heats a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and puts it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the anus; and does this two or three times, so that you know that these charred hairs are burned, which are similar to a bird’s feather; and then treats the moist tents with butter, until those hairs come out, then treats the wound with greasy ointment and bandages.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If he is thus healed, this is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent is not perforated as far as the finger in its base, and between your finger and the tent there is a thick covering of flesh or pus, and you see the fistula following this covering from the heart; then cut from the beginning of the fistula, and always push the tent forward, and then cauterize afterwards, until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be delivered and fall out; then wash away those foul flesh pieces that resemble a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the pus overcomes you, and runs between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or caustic medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 Because the fire cautery accomplishes two good things: that is to say, the burning of these hairs, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then cure the wounds moistened in butter or crushed substances, until the place gives pus, and then the burned hairs exit with the pus; then treat the wound with adhesive plasters made of hard charred material, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	 For when it is restored, it heals and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	 And if a fistula extends all the way to the anus, and is distant from the body, then you should insert your finger into the anus, and inquire there.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the wound, and between two there is a membrane or hair or charred material, if it is near bursting, then do not proceed except by way of trust and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can you put in patches and treat it as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the tissue that holds the anus, and cause excrement to pass by itself without will; then treat, as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or you remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut near the anus, with a probe or another appropriate instrument; then clean that charred material that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to prevent the fistula from returning to the part beyond the anus: this will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes fistulas occur in this manner: and it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, which is located on the side of the anus near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	 And you insert a twisted thread into it, and insert the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is spreading along the edge of the anus inside, then extract the thread from that hole, as you insert your finger into the anus; and pull out the end of the thread, and bring together the two ends, and press them against each other, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes restrain it, until the threads cut through those fleshy parts between them, and come out; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	 If the fistula does not burst, then make it burst in every way that you can, unless it is too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it is not necessary to make the covering for the ligation so deep, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the sharp thorn used to make the fistula is very pointed and cutting on one side, and not on the other, so that you do not cut what should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	 hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are in two ways: either they are inside the anus like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and blood always comes out of them, and there is one or several, and they are outside the anus and at the edge of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes come out a little citrine water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh. And the treatment for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to strain to go into the chambers until the anus protrudes, and the threads are visible; then hurry up and take it with tongs, or hold it with your nail, then cut at its roots; and if the nails cannot hold it because of moisture, take them in a cloth or in cotton, or in a piece of camlet; and pull them towards you with your hands, then cut, and sprinkle some hot powders on top that are suitable for cauterization; or cauterize as said in the chapter on cauterization, then treat with other treatments until they are healed; and if the anus cannot protrude, then give the patient a clyster of biting and harsh clyster to clean what is in the anus, so that it can come out clearly; when the patient strains, and the threads are out of the anus, the treatment is light; and it is that you take them with your nail or tongs, and cut, then treat as we have said, until they are healed, and that the patient fears incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If you must bring the stitch according to this manner: take a thread, pass it through a needle, then draw the thread out from above and make the needle pierce through from the other side; turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and let it be wide; hold the thread tightly, then knot the thread, pull out the needle, and do this with all the others, leaving one for the superfluous blood to flow out; then place on top a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, place it on top, and instruct the patient to rest; and leave it until they heal, and when they have healed, treat them with ointment and other treatments until they are cured.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 Of dryness of the intestines or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 Often occurs dryness in the intestines, by constraint of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine has no effect.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then it is necessary that you scrape the surface with a spatula or your fingernail, so as not to let it moisten; then heal it until it becomes dry as it should; and if it cannot dry, repeat the scraping more strongly than before, so that it bleeds a lot and scabs; then heal it until it is healed.
dou fremit	 of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Formica is a small furry creature that goes very deep into the body; sometimes coldness finds it, and one feels it like a deathly trembling, and it affects the whole body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is such that you take a quill from a goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place this quill on the trembling part, so that the circle encompasses the trembling entirely; then turn your hand with all the quill until you encircle the trembling completely, and insert it deeply, and pull out the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see this, do it with a quill of brass or iron in the same way, and let it be sharp below and smooth above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 nor should it be perceived, to keep at two fingers' width, and press hard. And if you see this, then cauterize the trembling part, as described in the previous chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or gold, or of melted tin or iron; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Therefore, those for whom one prepares in the care of children who are weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The form of the small and large enema is like this: the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and let there be an outlet where the belly is tied, as you see, and the head is pierced inside; and on one side let there be two holes, and on the other one hole; and the belly in which the medicines are placed should be made of a beast’s bladder or parchment, and it should be punctured all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one finger’s width, then insert into these holes a strong thread twisted into an X or circle shape, and tie the belly together like this: ; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then administer the enema; and that is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the enema not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg white, or similar substance, then insert it lightly; then the minister squeezes it with both hands together until it is all emptied, then remove the enema, and lift the patient's legs against the wall, and if the enema wants to exit, then hold it as long as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, then there is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you administer an enema for illness of the belly, and the enema is eager to exit, then repeat it until it is cleaned out.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are hemorrhoids or an abscess in the rectum, then let the enema be as thin as through a child's finger; and this is the form of the thin enema that draws the skin tight:
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have already spoken in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will speak about the treatments of hands and of medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by the falling of a stone, and by the cutting of a sword or knife, or by a spear or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the foot, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, for their treatment will come in its own chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from the fall of a stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is large, and you suspect heated abscess: then make the patient bleed immediately from the cephalic vein itself if there is little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite the injured part; and the patient should avoid excessive consumption of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if heated abscesses come there, cotton soaked only in rose oil or in stiptic wine; and if there is no heated abscess, then put on the fresh wound, all its blood not moved by the air, a powder that I will mention shortly; and if the heat has moved it, then apply some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large, such as from a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then join them by stitching, as I will say for wounds in the belly, about stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone and gaping, and only holds together by a single point, then shave it; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as heads and cooked grain, also like chickpeas, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find rottenness in the skin, and it reaches to the bone, then shave all the rot away, and throw it out, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped by cutting, and it cannot be stanched with medicines, then seek the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which seals before the heat has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is thus: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and make it into a fine powder, and fill the wound, and bind it strongly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this only with coal, when one has neither frankincense nor dragon's blood, but the heat has moved the wound.
