Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the heat has moved the wound, even if it is summer, do not apply this powder to it; but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey, until it casts off pus; then proceed with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you later about the breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	 of a neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other treatment than to leave it alone and not apply anything constricting, for this harms the nerves and causes them to shrink; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member. But let the medicine be warm, like hot water in soft water, mixed with rose oil, and washed similarly in soft water, and other stones of this kind according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, then stitch it up and bind it with bandages, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and there is swelling and they are full of pus, then pierce them in a lower place; and if an artery is cut and bleeding follows, then desiccate it, and let it flow out, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage is blocked so that food cannot pass, then sew up the windpipe on the skin of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for some days, and then treat it with drying compresses until it heals; and if there is an impression in the bone, then probe it; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them out completely if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound putrefies, and let it drain and close the opening; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 Et s'il a en la plaie os et il y a fistule, soignez-la ainsi que j'ai dit dans ce chapitre.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a wound from a spear or knife, and the wound is deep, observe if there are gas bubbles when the patient inhales: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not apply the powder at the first hour, nor bind it tightly for fear of drawing blood in too deeply, which may return to the heart and kill the patient; but apply an astringent ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton into the wound to absorb moisture, and make the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more; this way, there will be no spasms, nor heart tremors, nor difficulty in breathing; and when you see the bones set properly, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure it then with poultices and other treatments until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and works, know that there is a fistula; treat it as needed.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut and it is simple, either in the breast or back, then treat it as one would treat that which is in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is close to the bone and has splintered pieces, then cleanse the wound, and draw out the fragments if they are accessible; and if they are not accessible, then let the wound suppurate, which will ease extraction; and of other wounds on other limbs the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 Of the belly's dislocation
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The dislocation of the belly is large and medium and small; from a large wound sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, exit due to which their reinsertion is difficult; and the suture is more troublesome, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because it is more difficult to reinsert the intestines if they are not replaced immediately; for the intestine swells quickly when it feels the cold, so it enters more difficultly, and that is why the medium-sized wound is better, because one removes less of the intestine than in others. And know that the suturing of the belly is according to four manners: two common stitches occur in the suturing of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body, and there are two other specific stitches common to other wounds; however, they are more specific with regard to the suturing of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small, and something of the intestines has come out, it is a difficult thing to put back, which is done in one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten one sponge or one cloth in hot water only, or boil in vinegar and pepper and cloves, and bathe the intestine until the swelling is gone; sometimes this wine is constricting, and it is better to use alone for reducing swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling go away, moisten the intestine in hot water where althea and mallows have been boiled, for by this it is made easier to enter a little; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is better than cutting, for no one should cut there without great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting it: cut inside on the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out, then set them back in place according to their natural form in their proper location, if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the abdomen, you must make the patient lie on their back, and place their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the upper part of the abdomen, place the head and the feet higher than the lower parts, and likewise if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two parts, set your intention so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must administer this for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, use what you have prepared. Then take in your hands the pious minister who can hold all the stitching on his hand, and bring together the lips of the wound; this is the common manner of sutures, and it is that you take a needle or several, according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' width from the top of the wound, and there insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; pierce through the two heads of the leather with the two points of the syphac, which is under the leather inside, as much as you can make it pierce through that part, and bring together the two heads of the syphac, four together; then strain a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two lips of the wound accordingly, and then leave two fingers' width, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need of needles, until all the wound is contained; let the needles be moderate, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well: therefore they must be moderate; and it is not necessary to push the needles too deeply into the flesh and leather, lest they cut and work the wound before the suture; then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not injure the patient while sleeping, and place caps or bandages on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because one can use a single needle or two in the second suture, which is common, and it is that you bring together the two heads of the leather and the two heads of the syphac together at a needle where there is a strong moderate thread; and when you have pierced these four heads together, remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that one sews cloths; and place between each suture the thickness of a small finger; this suture is known by men, and I stitched a wound that a man had in his belly, which was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm in length, and it protruded from the intestines by about two palms in length, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestines to him after they had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed for fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I placed old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching: take the needle and insert it from the outer part to the inner part; when it has pierced the center straight on, leave the end of the silk or thread where you inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inner part to the outer part; and the intention of this stitching is that you sew just as furriers sew furs, and that you leave the silk once on one side and take it up again on the other side, until the stitching is entirely complete. etti
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, which Galen correctly identifies, is done as some do: they naturally join the two parts together and apply one end of the thread to the other end in this manner: take a needle with its tip near the mirror, and make it pierce that place only, leaving the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part until the inner part, at the two ends of the thread; then make it pierce one and the other from the outer part until the inner part, in two other places on the mirror which are on either side; and this is the best method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens so said this word, and some attest to it, that one should sew the belly with two needles, each having thread; and one must insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the stitching is in the middle of the belly, the suture is more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the fire has moved it, put back the intestines and the stitch; then place a powder that is good for flesh, and if the fire has moved it, place some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and let the threads be drawn out, and the silk and the bandage be bound together; then treat the wound like other wounds, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, as soon as it begins to heal, place old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 Because you do not need any other medicine in many situations when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may affect the principal members, then it is necessary for you to soak a light linen cloth in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the belly, which often happens, then administer an enema of black wine heated, and likewise if the putrefaction reaches the intestines; perforate them from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeune" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the thinness of its walls, and the delicacy of the whole body, and its close proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the intestine protrudes from the wound, reset it like an intestine while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned black or dark, then you must tie the black area to prevent blood flow, for there are veins and arteries; then cut that which is between the ligatures, and place the two ends hanging from the lower part of the wound until further relief during the extraction when the intestine falls back into the wound.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the boiling water
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is broken and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw a man wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became festered and turned into a fistula, from which came excrement and wind; I applied treatment as best I could, and did not cease to refine until he was healed, and the place cured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it solder, I feared that the patient had an ailment in his belly; and there was no ailment, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in such a manner: take large-headed needles, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the needle has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it draws its mouth up; and then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot untie, then place another needle after in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is seized; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 That chief so attaches itself in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the end of this intestinal thread that is very thin, then tie to this thread's end a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread in the needle, and sew the intestine, and bring it back together; and this method of stitching for the intestines is nothing more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal veins, there is no cleverness or skill, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 de fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a fistula, and similarly when it is cut open and returns to its natural state.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And according to the truth, fistula is defined as a hard and white swelling that is not painful, and it is open like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it flows clearly, and other times thickly; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and has no flesh, is only cured through one of the nine causes: that is to say, because of the insufficiency of blood or flesh; or due to its bad quality; or because there is hard flesh inside, on the lips, which prevents new flesh from growing; or there is too much moisture; or the place is rotten and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine used for healing is not good; or because the corruption is a form of pestilence; or due to the region's property, digestion is slow, healing is delayed, and it is naturally swollen; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 Or it is necessary for me to make you know the cure of fistula which is made by the work of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from the great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the sinus, or the intestine, or the bladder, or some of the ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and there is such that comes to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grievous sanation, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, take a probe of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, probe it; and if the fistula is crooked, seek it with a subtle probe of boxwood, for boxwood bends more easily around the curvature; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture goes from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then probe it wisely as best you can, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and it is hollow throughout, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels at the pressure of your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, cut according to what I have said, and remove firmly the foulness and corrupt flesh that is inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from a straight place, it is necessary that you cut deeply, as much as you can, then put in wet probes soaked in astringent medicine, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which remains at the bottom; and then put on dressings of fresh flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, burn it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupt from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve is injured in the main limb, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then clean it so that all the corruption is removed, then treat the charring flesh until it is healed; and if it does not heal, and returns again as before, know that you are not at the source: uncover and search until you reach the source, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a little bone corrupted, and you can pull it with tongs, draw it with an appropriate instrument; and if there are many bones, draw them all, leaving none; and if moisture hinders you, and there is no error or fear, cut and remove the moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 Et si tu ne les peux oster à une heure, mets sur la plaie quelque chose qui enflamme la pourriture, et laisse tant que le lieu soit pourri autour des os, et alors les os auront plus facilement; et s’il s’agit d’un gros os, comme de jambe ou de cuisse, il suffit seulement de retirer la corruption jusqu’à ce que toute la noirceur soit enlevée, puis referme la plaie; et s’il y a une grande partie de corrompu, et qu’elle atteigne la moelle de l’os, alors il faut brûler et couper tout jusqu’à la corruption, et ensuite le soigner jusqu’à ce qu’il soit guéri; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui arriva à un homme dans sa jambe, afin que tu en prennes exemple et aide dans ton travail.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 It was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause such that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason for it to be opened; but the physicians in their foolishness worked on it so much that the abscess burst open, and many matters were flowing out of it, and a fistula formed, and there were many holes from which all threw pus and moisture from the body; and many physicians treated him for about two years, and there was no sage in the art among them, until I was called to see it, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what was flowing through the holes of a large body; and the young man's flesh turned red and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that some come together from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hastened then and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, which I found to be rotten and perforated, with corruption reaching all the way to the inside of the bone; I removed what appeared to me of the rotten bone, thinking that there was no other corruption except what I removed. Then I began to treat the wound with drawing medicines for a long time, but it could not heal. So I started again and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, which I removed, and then I endeavored to heal the place; but I could not do so, because I cut around a palm's width of the bone, drawing it out all the way. Then I treated it with medicines again; and it healed and joined quickly, and I had no need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation of blood he often coughed up, but he was completely healed, and in place of the bone grew hard flesh, which was well-disposed and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be sutured in this manner: take a thread, and tie it to the end of the bone that is exposed; and command someone to extend it upwards; and put another thicker linen thread on top of the flesh above the bone, and stretch the end, so that you draw the rotten flesh below, and uncover the flesh in the place where you want to suture, so that the suture does not hurt the flesh; and place a piece of wood or a board under the bone to better cover the rotten flesh; and one must suture as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and suture again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a log underneath, and then saw from one part to the other the corruption, and let the saw be as long as the corruption I said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut the corrupt joint, and saw the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other way than to cut; and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand or in the sole of the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nevertheless you must seek out this corruption, how it opens to you; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, except that the vein or nerve should not hinder you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each type of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the methods of diseases; so consider the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	 Of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head rots either from within or from without; and when you have treated that rotting with the cure of medicines, and they do not help at all, then you must cut off that limb up to the place where the rotting comes, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the lack of the limb. And the sign of this is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and rots after the blackness; then goes that rot from limb to limb, and spreads throughout the body; so hasten to cut off, and if it is from the sting of some poisonous animals, such as a sea scorpion or snake and similar things, if the rotting is at the top of the arm, cut it off, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut it with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and no healing will help except by the power of God; and do the same when the corruption comes to the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it climbs the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it reaches above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the patient die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is such that you bind it above and below, and extend a band downward and another band upward, and you remove the flesh between the two bands to one broad spatula, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or saw, and place on each side a piece of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy part, and let the patient suffer other injuries and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if blood flows during your work, then cauterize the place quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed; and I will tell you that this happened to a man in our country: he had a blackness that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corruption first came into his foot, so much so that it spread throughout his entire foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover his foot, and was healed; and a long time after, the corruption returned to his hand, and he came to me, and I put repulsive things on him after cleansing his body, and could not stop the corruption; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, because I hoped to repel the matter; and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he would die, because the man's virtue was weak; and he became completely desperate, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have only told this story for those who may need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy place and stays so long that it causes a large gathering of pus; then it bursts and breaks open, and the pus spurts out, and the place remains empty, like an empty vessel; and the skin on top is as delicate as a well-cleaned cloth, and it does not extend to the bone or to the nerve. Such a disease is called "sinus," and it is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you can cut all around it, even when it is delicate, like a cloth; and it does not close due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you believe that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with an enema in this manner: observe if the breast is large, and the pus that comes out of it is foul-smelling, then enema with Egyptian medicine which is made as follows: take equal parts of aloes, oil, and lead, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of this according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and enema the breast, plugging the orifice; leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed; sometimes use an enema of ashes-water, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, pour water over them, strain it, and enema until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ashes-water, then use an enema of water and honey in which there is a little ground lead; or use an enema of honey and wine mixed together, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the wound dry; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then enema with that which produces flesh in it, and it is that you take diafinit plaster, mix it with rose oil and wine; or use an enema of some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the treatise on ointments; and if the orifice of the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with iron, and insert a plug of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment until it is widened; and if the wound is too large, then sew it up, leaving only one place where the enema can enter, and if the orifice from which pus comes out is higher, then cut it lower.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the boil is fully ripe, do not let any flesh enter it; and if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then prepare in such a manner that the boil runs to the lowest place there is, for when the boil is fully ripe, do not let any flesh enter it. And if you cannot cover the breast below as you wish, then prepare in this manner: that the boil runs lightly downward and leaves nothing of the boil; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut at the edges around the hole of the breast a little wider than the first, then extend an ointment softly over another cloth according to the quantity of the hole, and put it on the hole of the wound to lighten the boil, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is on the hole of the breast, remove often to remove the boil, and know what comes out of the boil, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not. And when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that leaps onto the hole of the wound, know that the breast has already healed, and the health approaches; and then unbind it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you unbind the wound, then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the chest throws up undigested food after many days, know that the chest is not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons are excreted after a long time, do not despair of health, for the healthy state is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For there are men in whose wounds the meat takes a long time to heal, and of those who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes up from the chest after many days, know that the chest is not healed; and if the chest delays in healing, and it is distant, then apply dry medicines, moist in substance and dry in virtue, as the diaphoretic ointment does, for there is a great deal of vitriol in it, and it is the last medicine to use; take the diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and wash it with old wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and this same cooked, thickened thing does better when the diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and crush them, and powder them on honey as it is over the fire; and then glue a cloth, and place it on the chest; and sometimes they administer long aristolochia and celestial lily roots, which are like vetch flour and centaury; and use of simples or compounds: crush them, and make powder, and put on the honey I have mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or in hard members, or in the joints; so cure as for a fistula cure, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the fingernail abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 of the finger or toe is an abscess that occurs beneath the nail of the hand or foot, or sometimes in other fingers; and when it is neglected, and no attention is paid to it, a hot abscess develops, which runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and sometimes it runs the entire length of the nail; and corrosion occurs down to the bone, causing foul-smelling pain, and the end of the finger or toe is swollen, and the color is red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the section on incisions, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut off with an iron all the overgrowth that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to prick and wound it, then you must place a red-hot needle under the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it upwards, and carefully and lightly cut away the flesh; and put on top of the remaining flesh medicines that burn and corrode to remove everything; then treat with onion until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if there is corruption in the bone, cut it away and draw out strongly, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the tooth decay, cut it away from one side, as has been said before, then treat until it is healed; and if it is struck and swells and causes great pain, it is necessary that you first cleanse it; then cut the nail diagonally with a sharp spatula, ensuring that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something to soothe it.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two thumbs that sometimes grow in the hands of some men are all fleshy, and sometimes there is bone, and occasionally there is a nail, and sometimes they grow from the root of the joint, or the growth is in the middle of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 That which grows in any part of the thumb does not move, and that which grows at the joint of the thumb sometimes moves; the shape of the fleshy one is light, like this: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 That which grows at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; therefore, use the scoop.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In one who is born or should at the anus, it is necessary that you cut first the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable size for this, then cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The swelling that comes to the fingers together comes by birth, or by wounding, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Then you must cut this swelling, so that the fingers may return to their natural shape; then place between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so they do not swell; or you put between two thin slices of lead, until the place is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly one of his hands touches the palm with the hand, then cut that joint as it is needed.
des vils	 from the fingers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The veins are large, swollen and full of superfluous melancholic substances that come in many members of the body; and it happens more often in the legs of those who go on foot, work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer purging with cole, and then heal it with the balm of basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is according to two methods: one is that you cut them and draw out the black blood with a lance; and the other method is that you lift the vein and pull it all out with force.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The cutting is done in this manner: first raise the leg with very hot water until the large vein becomes subtle; then pull the patient's leg from above the thigh down to the part below the knee; then cut the vein in one of three places, with a wide incision; then lift and draw out strongly the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can bear; and then bandage it, and instruct him to feed on dark-colored foods; and repeat the evacuation and cauterization when the veins are full again, which is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The elevation of it is done in this manner: lift the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put him in a bath, and raise his leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins; and if you do not have a bath, heat it at the fire, and then cut towards the vein from the knee to the ankle; then lift the skin with a hook, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white rope; then push the blood downwards, so that it is raised from the skin, and then bandage it lightly with linen, then cut in another place above or below three times; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the hook as you have done before, and bandage it with another linen as you did first; then make another incision, or several if you need to, then lift it, and cut towards the toe of the foot, then draw and lift up to the second incision; then draw from incision to incision, until all comes out strongly, then cut; and if you cannot draw and lift it, put a strong double-threaded needle under it, and bandage and draw it, and put it under a linen cloth, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it is harmful to the patient; and when you have drawn all of it, put moistened wool in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must split it obliquely, but do not cut it; and draw it out as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The form of the iron with which one cuts the face is curved, and it does not cut deeply lest it cut the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is located in the legs, in hot areas where no grass or tree grows, and in dry earth; and by chance it may be found elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the putrefaction that comes under the skin, just as serpents and worms are injected between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 Et if the sign of the beginning of this vein is such that it comes in the leg a very great swelling, then changes the place, and begins the vein to come out, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, and amenistre au leu medicines injanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein there is less blood, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or in the foot, and much pus comes out of it, and from which it exudes blood; then treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 Worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This illness is called in our land "cattle disease", because it happens often to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes through the whole body ascending and descending, and one feels it well when going from member to member, until it tears the skin where it goes, and exudes pus; and it is generated by the putrefaction of some humors, just like come worms, snakes, leeches, and ascarids in the belly; and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: if you see it being cleaned and drawn out, one cannot do more than when it goes; therefore, you must bind the place above and below with a strong, tight ligature, then cut above and draw it strongly, and if the pus is deep in the flesh and you do not find it, burn it with fire on top until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the head of the eye, tightly hold the sorcil beneath it, then cut above, and draw it strongly; and one must use the patient for bodily cleansing with dissolving medicines for evil humors that cause putrefaction, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes to some members, and then moves from one member to another; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.
