I was called to a sick woman and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and a little later, I saw it rise up to the shoulder, faster than anything else, like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another; the pain left that spot and pierced the shoulder, and then a little later it ran through the whole body until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it was constantly going around the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 I was greatly amazed at how it moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this illness in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Nevertheless, I had seen many who had felt pain move from one place to another, but I had never seen it as I did in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and open veins, and for this reason these windy constrictions appear; and they are not apparent according to this reasoning in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and filled veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see this illness being treated and the patient feels this pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind it quickly above and below, and then cut into it until that constricted wind escapes; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then treat it as one would treat those who dispel winds, such as foul-smelling pills, and pills of serpentaria, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 Arrows are varied according to their appearances and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 Their diversity is such that there are some with large tips and small ones, barbed and smooth; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and when one strikes a member, it does so in two ways: in the principal members, as in the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it strikes therefore in any of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death follows in many cases; and when this bad sign does not appear, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the signs of the brain when an arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps the siphon which is above the brain, are dizziness, confusion, fainting, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and mixing of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is a discharge from the nose or the ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice; and from the wound there is white moist matter resembling pus, and also like brains; and if these signs appear to you, then abstain from the cure, and remove the arrow if it is not inside.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of the arrow when it hits the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and it feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood flows out, and coldness and cold sweat come, and fainting: know then without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the signs of the arrow that never leave are when there is no plain foam coming out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and pants heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And if the arrow falls into the covering of the chest, it is near the small ribs; and there is great pain and panting; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if the arrow falls into the stomach, perhaps some undigested flesh comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if the arrow falls into the belly, and some feces come out through the rectum, then there is no hope for a cure, nor for the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 Et si la flèche tombe dans la vessie, et l'urine jaillit par à-coups, et le patient ressent une douleur intense : sachez que la blessure est mortelle.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and backbone of the back and collarbone and thighs and legs, and similar members, are safe according to many arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you that happened to me so that you may do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to me that an arrow fell into the cheekbone at the root of the nose. I attempted [to remove it], and pushed it out from the other side under the fat of the ear, and was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And he shot an arrow in a game, which fell into the fat of the eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was blunt, so that he could only reach the point near the shaft, and the arrow was large from a Turkish bow, all the iron light without ears; the game was hunted, and no evil accident happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And he shot an arrow from the throat at a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears; I shaved the beard, and maneuvered until I shot it, and the Christian was hunted.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And he shot an arrow at a man, which had fallen in the belly, and I thought that he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and secured it, and drew it out strongly, and he had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And if you see a man in whom an arrow fell into the back, and the wound was healed over; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural disposition at all, nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And you see another man in whom an arrow fell into his face, and the wound was healed over; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I drew an arrow from one of the king's princes, which had fallen into his nose and was leaning slightly to the right side; and the arrow was completely encased in pus. I was called to the cure after it had fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 Si trouvai la plaie très étroite.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I found the wound very subtle, and did not feel it at all; but he felt a pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the point of the arrow. I applied a drawing plaster to prevent swelling; and then the wound made by the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I left the plaster on for less than a day, and the wound closed again, and the patient remained thus for a long time until he felt the arrow inside his nose; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for less than a day until it opened up; then I probed it and felt the head of the arrow which was lodged in place; afterwards, I continued to apply the same corrosive medicine to the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became visible; and it took about four months for the wound to heal enough that I could insert tongs, but they wouldn't grasp it properly; so I didn't stop trying and devising ways to extract it with various instruments until one day I managed to grasp it firmly with well-made tongs, as will be described at the end of this chapter, and I drew it out and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the doctors judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the method for extracting certain arrows; apply your care to those that I do not mention, for the book cannot contain everything. But a wise master understands well a small thing, and on what is present and defective, he finds new work, and nine instruments, in the treatment of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows should not be extracted from the members in which they are embedded except in two ways: either through the place where they entered, or through another part; and those that come out through the place where they entered are arrows entering fleshy places, and such sometimes nowadays.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not come out now, let it stay until the flesh is rotten around it, and the opening is widened; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, moving it each day; and then it comes out, and if it does not come out, pierce all around with a very fine instrument, until the place around is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and reaches one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned occur to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it is equal after some days, for if the arrow reaches the saphenous vein, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone, and does not reach as far as the marrow, and the patient remains for some days without bad consequences, draw out the arrow.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it is deeply lodged in this way and cannot be drawn out, then apply tarres around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is turned in the body so that one cannot see it, then search all over the patient; and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, then enlarge the wound until it is big enough; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has barbs that hold it in place, then remove the flesh that is impaled on either side as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow so that you can draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, for then you would draw it out more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the place around is rotten, then draw it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is unfavorable to you, then use the method we mentioned in the treatment chapter; and beware of cutting into the nerve or vein, and devise a way how you can safely draw out the arrow, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and position the patient as he was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do so, then position him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another place, where it sticks out or the skin is swollen such that one can see or feel it clearly: then cut around it until the pincers can grasp it, and then draw it out; if it is not drawn now, it will never be.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is lodged in the bone, then turn your hand smoothly until it enters the bone and enlarges the bone, then extract it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes forth strongly; and if the arrow's shaft is in it, push the whole shaft through; and if the arrowhead has fallen off, and you see that a pushing instrument should be used, apply a falling instrument so that the point of the arrow enters the notch of the instrument; and then push strongly, and if the arrow is hooked, insert the instrument with the point entering in, to lighten the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, it is necessary that you cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Et si la saiette tombe dans le pied ou dans l'abdomen ou dans la vessie ou dans les côtes, et elle est proche de la surface, alors tu peux couper dessus. Si tu coupes, fais attention de ne pas couper une veine ou un nerf; puis extrais la flèche, puis couds la plaie si nécessaire; et soigne-la jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit guérie.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The form of the pincers used to extract arrows resembles a bird’s beak, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape at the end of the pincers is like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 The shape of the tongs for pressing and holding is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	 of the common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 There are 31 veins from which one can be bled, of which there are 16 in the head. That is to say: two veins that are behind the ears and are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples; and the two veins that are in the two eyebrows of the two eyes and are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two jugulars that are in the neck; and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, which are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed are V in each arm: one is the cephalic and is located on the left side, and common people call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fascium", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is also on the right side, and common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the ulnar, and it is that one from which we heal, which clearly appears on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The salavatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and the foot there are three veins: one is under the wrist of the left side, and the second saphena which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "nasse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears is beneficial for old cathartics and headaches; and the quality of the bleeder, as I tell you, is that you grasp the patient's head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then the patient tightens his neck with a screw until two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places from the head: seek them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, let it go; then take the lancet, and push it beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein, and cut through the skin and the vein very well two fingers wide across, and make the blood come out until you wish; then press and bind it, until it is healed; and I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good for an old migraine, and a headache, and a customary blindness, and for the body of tears in the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeder are as I say: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins appear clearly; and feels the pulse beneath your finger, and then sign with ink; then lifts the heart upon the vein high to your finger's tip, and pushes the lancet underneath, and raises the vein high, and cuts it, as you have done in the other two veins, and makes the blood flow according to your need; then releases the patient, and puts your finger on the vein for an hour, then puts cotton on top; and then bandages it well, and leaves it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their cutting and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose,
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 Deffentement, si li malaides a ceste maladie desous la poine et en dessus et alant sus les oreilles, dont chelui qui a tel maladie fait tantost li voinne, car li saines ne puet mie estre bonnes se le os sont malades.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 And if the flame is subtle, perhaps it breaks; then make blood flow, as much as you need, and then bind with a bandage, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The bleeding from the vein of the nose is good for fever and madness, and for facial illnesses such as migraine and redness that occurs in the face, and especially when it is chronic; and the quality of the bloodletting is that the patient strains his neck, then presses his nose against your left hand, and takes a long, subtle flame, and sticks it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well in itself, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne,
de la sainie des leivres	 Of liver bleeding
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 Liver bleeding on the lips above helps to heal wounds in the mouth, and prevents gum decay, and heals lip cracks, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of liver bleeding are to have the patient sit before you, and grasp his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two wounds, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized because they are black, and around them there are small black veins: therefore cut both of these, and if you do not recognize them and are in doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and do the same for the two wounds that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the wound beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The wounds under the tongue aid after the wound of the cephalic [vein], and this is for the constriction of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the sanguineousness is such that the patient lies between your hands in front of the sun, and he raises the tongue, and looks underneath on each side a black wound: therefore, heal one and the other, but not too deeply, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The wounds of the knife with which one commonly bleeds are bled according to two manners: either by pricking with all the flame of a wide and broad lancet, or with an olive-shaped sharp [lancet] like cutting knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and sharp according to the width and narrowness of the wounds.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The form of the flame is very renowned, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary for opening the filled veins full of thick and visible blood, which contain thick and turbid blood; and this is the olive-shaped flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 And it is more delicately pointed, and it is for bleeding the delicate veins, where there is delicate citrine blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The bleeding from the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed wisely, and to guard against the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery, and blood flows out, then it must be cauterized, as I have said; and the flame should not be pointed but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, then you must restrain it and change another one; or seek any branch of it, or heal in its place the vein in the middle of the arm: it opens clearly; and cut with a knife-like flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to recognize the place of the bleeding, then first restrain the arm so that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with a knife-like flame; and beware not to strike the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is of the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, and ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, and ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	 Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, and il te vaint, and li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’ele apert, car li chefs de li retraient; and estainche li sans.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a peel of fig, and cut it, and take one half and bind well up to the next day; if the blood clots, that is good; if not, then cure it as we have said, with powders that clot blood; and clotting is not harmful in many conditions due to the small area of the wound, and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps so that it draws blood from above and below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the bleeder to be careful not to penetrate too deeply into the nerves beneath, and if he finds the nerve, it swells up and the healing may be harmed, and perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you should bleed with an insensible instrument; and avoid the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then incise it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The vein of the cephalic (also known as the great saphenous vein) is helpful because it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and one must incise sharply at the olive branch vein or the myrtle branch vein, for it is the safest of all veins, since beneath it there is neither nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 However, one must seek the lightest place, and it is not serious if one misses the first time, and one starts again; and perhaps the place swells in some men when one misses the first time, but it is not serious.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the incision depends on your intention.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about bloodletting is that it is not practiced except to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are known: cephalic, fast, and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring, autumn, and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, two hours or three into the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The bloodletting done for illnesses has no fixed time, but only when necessary, day or night, at all hours and in all seasons; and one should not bleed children under fourteen years of age, nor pregnant women except after the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 They should not be healed, the old who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 And when someone wants to be healed in whatever manner, it is necessary that he purges the intestines with a light enema if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines the harmful superfluities into the principal members; nor should one heal who is too full of food, or drunk to the point of being weak, or dropsical; and one should not undertake healing after a colic attack, vomiting, purging of the belly, increased intercourse with women, hard work, vigil, fasting, and whatever totally weakens the strength, either by something of the weapon or of the body; then subtilize the humors if the blood is thick, by food and drink and medicines if you have the power; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and heal from the vein of the foot around the third hour, as we have said; and guard yourself that day against work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be joyful and glad, and let the healer be higher than he whom you heal, and rub his arm two or three times, then draw the ligament moderately, for if it is too tight or lax, the blood cannot flow well; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then the healer moistens the flame with a little old oil, then places his right thumb on that vein below the place where he wants to heal, so that the vein does not burn and rupture during healing.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 Because there are veins that flow like cords to the healer, and some that are full of air, so that when one raises the flame, it draws back from the flame, and one cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow. Therefore, the healers must be knowledgeable in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 And if the vein opens on the first attempt, it is good; if not, then one must start again a little below that spot or quickly above, if the spot is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the spot is swollen and the patient is frightened, let him rest for one day or two, and do not tie the arm: perhaps pustules will come; do not bathe in hot water, then resume the bloodletting if he wishes; and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that enough blood will flow as you want, then drive the flame straight into that same opening; and work a little quickly, before the spot swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not begin the bleeding again, and put some lye of oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and it is the lye that is used in this place like oil; and thus administer the lye of oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same acts as a triple and bow when placed on the site; so subtilizes the blood and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if a large abscess forms, which often happens, especially when it is not strongly bled except for that time when the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put on the site a sponge moistened in water and salt, a little warm, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if any blackness or greenness remains at the site after some days, it does not harm; and if you see, put on some aloes or myrrh dissolved in calamint juice, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 And many times an abscess and appearance occur at the wound of the basilica: place your hand upon it, and if you find the spot soft to the pressure of the hand, then that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, do not place any of the things we have mentioned upon it, for by chance some blood from an artery may come out; but make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw from each vein according to the quantity of its strength, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary for the one who is strong and healthy, if he needs bloodletting, to make a wider wound and let the flame be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and he should be bled little and often, and he must be bled by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from bleeding too much or cutting nerves, and it is better than long or wide bleedings.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And for the one whose body is lacking in bloodletting, it is necessary to give him moist bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is heated, draw blood three or four times. If he has a cold temperament, before bleeding, let him eat moist bread soaked in honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he faints at the bloodletting, after the loss of much blood, then it is necessary that he drink broth made from meat and a subtle scented syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to bleed from one arm, and bloodlet again later, then it is necessary that when he is weakened by great bloodletting, he should bleed a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength, continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And if he wants to bleed from one arm after the first bloodletting, and he is strong of body, then let him bleed seven hours after the first bloodletting, or in the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And whoever wants to heal from another place, must do so on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood within the body that is already heated, and it causes fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening until it flows in streams; then you check all the conditions of healing, and place your hand on the pulse when he heals, so that death does not come in place of the stream, and this often happens when the healer is negligent; and it should not be done when you see the arm being freed, and blood comes out a second time, and the opening is closed, then you press very firmly; nor if it is curved, let him quickly extend his arm, for that would be bad; but leave it until it heals a second time; or you prick with the point of the flame, until the frozen blood at the vein's mouth comes out in streams, and place a little cloth soaked in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrain it, until the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, heal it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The vein in the middle of the arm is healed in the place of the head's vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of healing is such that the patient places their hand in hot water until the blood vessel becomes red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears clearly, then heal it now across, not broadly or lengthwise; and let the opening be wide, and heal close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, then put the hand back in hot water, and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, because one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the healing of this vein is safer than any other veins, as there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The bleeding of the little finger of the right hand is good for all liver diseases, and this is how you do it: grasp the hand, and immerse it in hot water until the vein swells, if you can see it; and if the blood flows crookedly, and you cut all around, it will not cause harm; but do not go too deep, because the nerves are underneath all the bare skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn blood as much as you need, then place oil and silk on the vein to close it quickly, and do this for each time.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The wound on his left hand is as valuable as the disease of the mice, and does everything just as I told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The wound on the sole of the foot is as valuable as all the diseases that are under the body, such as marsh fever, and retention of urine, and disease of the kidneys, and ancient hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of his wound is such that the patient should step in hot water, and rub on the wound until it opens, and bind above the ankle; and the wound is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; then heal where the largest vein is, or at the ankle, for that is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	 And if you make an incision on the foot, beware of the nerves that are below it, and make the incision crosswise like in cutting; and let the flame be calm.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water, and let the wound drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the incision fails the first time, then repeat it a second time above a little bit, because the place is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the sole of the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place for the incision of sciatic pain is at the ankle of the leg, and its incision relieves the pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 Et les qualités de sa saignée sont telles que le patient entre dans le bain, et il tire quatre doigts au-dessus de la cheville en tordant, car autrement la veine n'ouvre pas; et s'il ouvre, alors il saigne dans toutes les manières possibles, y compris en traversant; et il est préférable que tu le coupes, car l'endroit est sec, et cela fonctionne bien pour de nombreux hommes.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 Et si tu ne trouves pas la veine, alors saigne un membre du patient qui est ouvert sur le dos du pied, vers le petit doigt, en prenant garde aux nerfs; fais couler autant de sang que nécessaire, puis délie le lien et mets un coton dessus, en le serrant; elle est maintenant saignée.
des sainies de ventouse	 of the cupping glass
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Cupping glasses are made of horn, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: by striking to draw blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this cupping which is without striking is done in two ways: with fire or without fire; and the cupping which is done by striking and drawing blood is done in fourteen places on the body, of which one is entirely at the top of the head; and another is in the middle of the neck; and two others on each side of the neck; and a cup under the chin; and a cup on each shoulder; and a cup on the buttocks; and cups in the middle of the two arms; and cups on the two legs; and cups on the two ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken anyone, as is done with venesection; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from excess, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if due to illness it is necessary to bleed, or by habit, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, and at the end, and in between, and every time; for there are such people that when they need to bleed, their head becomes heavy; and there are those who find swelling and redness on their face, and on their head, and on their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and vomit blood; and there are those who dream, and see through the night bleeding and wounded and dead things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order to bleed every three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The flow of the nose also helps to relieve the heaviness in the head ... which affects the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of the entire body; and this venting is in place of the cephalic vein, and it is not appropriate for those of cold temperament to use it, or those who have catarrh, because it causes them great harm; and therefore, it is not appropriate for the elderly to use it, nor those with cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And those who frequently blow their nose become oblivious, and because of this, it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The venting in the neck is in place of the sinecure of the head and basilica, and therefore it is good for constriction of the foot, and fissure of the throat passage, and for coughs, and for abdominal distension; and there one should apply it sparingly, because if it stays too firmly, it may cause oblivion in the stomach or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 The inflammation below the chin is for diseases of the mouth, and for the decay of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 The inflammation of the shoulders is for diseases caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The inflammation of the ribs is as effective as that of the three main veins of the arm, because it attracts blood from these large veins; and instruct the practitioner not to pierce too deeply into the flesh, because this place is without muscle and lies beneath nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	 The cupping glass placed on the buttocks is for hemorrhoids of the anus and for diseases below, and it must be large and made of copper so that it can draw well; and if by chance it were delicate, it would break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 The cupping on the legs is clearly effective, for they draw blood from the entire body, and are valuable for ancient pains of the kidneys, and the womb, and the bladder, and they remove the flowers; and they are placed on the II sophenes, and the II ankles, yet after long use, they weaken the body, and bring about paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	 The way to apply the cupping is as follows: first, place it empty and quickly suck, and put it on hastily, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and open the blood vessels of the blood; then prick, and reapply the cups, and take care in the condition of the body, for there are such who have dark flesh and clear pores: thus it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and deep enough; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 And if the vein is large, one must strike twice: the first time to make the blood flow finer.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And if the vein is very thick, one must strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, it suffices to prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want a lot of blood, we prick often; and if the vein is thick, we strike deeper, and the result is that the heart is suddenly pierced, which is necessary for those with thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow. One must anoint the places of the cupping glasses with an opening and dissolving oil: in summer, with violet oil or oil of sweet almonds or oil of cucumber seeds; and in winter, with oil of watercress, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the excess is thick and cold, take oil of bitter orange, or balm, or oil of aniseed, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one whom we are treating has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied there, but it must be washed afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or water of black nightshade, or water of cucumber, or water of purslane, or other similar ones.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And if there is much moisture, then it should be raised with alum, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have thick excesses should be raised with old wine, or water of sow thistle, or decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things; and one must not apply a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and they should not sleep after cupping, and it is necessary that he wash himself, when he wants to be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And warn if the person who is healing is of a choleric nature, and if his blood is too hot and inflamed; then he must take cold things, such as crab apples and endives and lettuces in water, and similar things; and he should eat pears, and meat from a goat, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And he who has a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and wine of medium scent, which is between old and new, and eat pears, and apples, and small birds and thrushes; and on the day that he will be ventosed, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes a tranquilizer or musk before ventosing, or after, to strengthen the main members; and the blood should be refined, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The cupping glasses that are placed without pricking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the bladder, and on gout, and on the belly and the vulva and the loins and the hip, because these members do not tolerate being pricked on their eyes, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we place them on the breasts when the milk flows; to remove the thickness that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and the vulva to reduce the member; and it removes the pain, when there is a swelling or stone, sometimes it removes the swelling by its attractive power, or it dries out the stone from its place; and so it does when placed on the liver and bladder when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a manner that one fills the cupping glass with heated water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	 The form of the cupping vessel administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And let there be two fingers of width and half a palm of depth, and let it have on its circumference around the middle one small hole, like to insert a needle, and let it be of copper, smooth beforehand so that it does not harm the patient when placed upon the limb; and let there be in the middle a rod of copper or iron across which to place a heated cloth, both large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who use them; for the cups of children are different from those of the elderly, and of the thin from the fat.
