Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two ulnae", one of which is small, and that is the one that follows the elbow; and the other is large, and that is the one below, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large ulna breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small bone is broken, the restoration is easy, and so is the healing; and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more serious than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small bone that is broken, then you should extend it slightly and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large bone, then you must pull it more firmly; and extend it on a pillow, and hold the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the pillow in front of him higher, so that the patient feels no labor. Then the attendant should extend his arm to the part below his hand or the wrist, and another attendant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then let the physician set it equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if in the break there are pieces, then place each one in its proper place; and if any of them is dislocated so that it touches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut above it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken about this in a separate chapter; thus take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the restoration there appear such abscesses, then place a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and bind the cloth above delicately, until these abscesses are appeased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the bandage, and put the plaster of mill powder with plenty of egg on it, then put on the splints, and let the splint of the break be always stronger, and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be VI splints on the arm in several positions: whether the break is in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more tightly over the break than elsewhere, and always less in distance, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are over the break be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And bandage the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any evil occurrence happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you should wash the limb with hot water until the itching is soothed; and let the limb rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the binding, and if the ligament is weakened and the bone dislocated, or similar thing, treat it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if you fear that nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you should soften it with a poultice, and leave it thus for some days until the nourishment flows, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things happens to the patient, then do not release him until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 And if he is in a state where his hands are on his neck and they are even, and he guards against movement and dislocation, and sleeps on his back; know that this breakage will be restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the strengths and temperaments of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that on the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers, breakages occur rarely, and only bending happens frequently.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the base of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to sit in a cross-legged position and sit upright facing forward evenly; then he places his hand on an extended table, and the servant extends the broken bones, and the doctor makes them even until they are well joined; and applies a poultice and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then place a splint according to the size of the location; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is around the stomach near the sole of the foot, make a sphere of cloth, and instruct the patient to tie it to their broken foot; and then tie with a long cloth, and let the knot be as large as the palm of the hand, and tie it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the break is in the finger, it is necessary that you place a bandage above, and another below on the foot, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind the whole hand, and secure the knot between the two fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the break occurs in any of the fingers, if it is a fracture, set it straight as needed; and bind with the foot, and if you see it, place a small straight bandage to lift the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in other fingers, such as the thumb or others, set it straight, and tie with the healthy finger that follows; either tie all together at once, whatever works best, or place a bandage above, as with the thumb; and take care in restoring and treating the abscess, and support those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 Of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it is clearly seen when it turns forward or backward; and the restoration is done by tying one ligament above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches his ligament equally to his side; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the base of the thigh, then one of the ligaments should be toward the knee, and the other ligament below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And so if it is near the knee, then the ligament should be next to the knee, and the extension downward; then let the doctor place the bone equally in his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice, and bandage it, unless pus comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, leave it to heal before returning to your work and care; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary that you wrap around the break II or III layers of thick bandages, leaving excess material, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the knee, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and bring the ends of the thread above; then turn the bandage over the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the break, and place a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to make the compression even, then begin to bind strongly III or IV turns around the break; and as you go higher from the break, it tightens less; then take II ends of the thread that you have passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie III splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, so that you come near the foot; and tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, since neither abscess nor swelling nor other similar thing occurs.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, then dislocate it, and address what comes there, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, then one must remove them, if possible; and if not possible, then one must split the place, and draw strongly; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 And sometimes the thigh is broken in such a way that stakes are put into it, as in the shoulder and in the arm; nevertheless, in this restoration the patient does not limp.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored in five days, or a little less or more, according to the diversity of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 from the tendon of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee hollow, there is little fracture, but it often bends.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a split or hole, and this happens in any wound, and without wound, and everyone feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the healing is such that one puts equal what is round to its two [parts], as long as they can be assembled; then apply the poultice, and put on a round bandage if you need it, and bind it as necessary, then follow all the procedures we have said in other fractures, just like an abscess or similar things; for each incident, apply what is needed until healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are II bones, of which one is rightly called "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and every fracture happens as it does in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the workings are all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the subtle bone is broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it is easily seen; and it turns below.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction, and set it straight, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several fragments, then the traction should be less and lighter; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the breakage of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle there is no breakage, but sometimes the bones of the foot break and at two places, and it happens more often with fractures in several parts.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if there is breakage of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, then put the patient's foot on the ground as if they were about to walk, and now place your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their place; then apply a plaster and wool on top, and place under the sole of the foot a small flat plate with two full holes, then bind the foot properly, after you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, then unbind the bandage, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if there are any broken fingers, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and it should be a little wider, then place under the foot this board that I have mentioned, and secure it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken fingers, place on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen cloth, and secure the board under the foot; and let it stand at the head of the board outside the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each case accordingly.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the bone in the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the female’s natural passage is broken, let her sit enlarged, then incline it to the back part, and hold it from behind; then fill the natural passage of the female with cotton, putting in as much as a finger's length; then raise the woman and lift up the back little by little, and then the cotton jumps until it comes to the entrance of the natural passage, and the bone returns with the finger; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or so: thus the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a reed through its opening, then blow into the bladder until it is inflated inside; thus the natural passage will return to normal; then fill it with cotton and leave it that way for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bones of the fist of a man are broken, or of a woman, restore them as we have said concerning the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from those who put their study and practice into it, and pay attention to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the fracture signifies in several ways the right way of restoration; understand this well.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose quill and put the penis into it; then wrap cloths around it, and leave it there for three days or so, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for someone with a fracture and wound, especially if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be bled now, just like the wounds we have mentioned testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound is healthy, then close it with vitriol, if you have nothing else. Then begin again to restore the fracture in that same hour, or that day, if pus does not develop there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if pus develops there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring on evil results.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is visible under the skin, then it is necessary that you place your hands lightly on either side of it with slight pressure.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if you are not prepared to place it equally with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument which has seven or eight inches in length, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this reason it is necessary that the surgeon have three or four, according to what he needs for each fracture cure; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the end, and thicker towards the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," because the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it back once, until it returns, and let them be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument may have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot bring the bone back as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument for this purpose, either a knife or a saw; then scrape away the roughness and small splinters that remain in the bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is done so that it is in its place, then moisten the bandage in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put on the wound any cerote or other oily substance, lest it bring forth putrefaction and corruption; then administer stars when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not constrained with the fracture; and many times have foolish physicians done this, and have brought death or corruption upon the patient sometimes; and let the constraint be gentler and softer than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or great, and you doubt that evil accident may occur, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not necessary to apply bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two days the wound swelling up, remove everything that you have put on it at all times, and apply a healing salve for wounds, such as tetrapharmakon salve and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the swelling flows down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot heal but returns again bowed, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must search the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, you must cure it according to what is said in the previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the thighbone or shoulder blade, and other similar large bones, do not pull it out, for many times death results from this, but leave it until it rots; by chance it will fall out by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 On bruises that come upon a sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see this after the health of the bruising, especially when it is near the joint, and seeing the limb’s appearance is unpleasant; and by chance, the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Take heed therefore if the nose is fresh: then administer stiptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others; so that you take one of these things or all together, and boil them with stiptic wine or with plenty of egg or with honey; and place it on the nose in bandages, and bind it well, and do not unbind for many days; then unbind, and begin another, until the swelling is gone; or you bind over a well-made piece of lead; for the properties of lead are such that they remove all the swellings from the members; and if the swelling has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, cut off the top, and bring out the apparent superfluity; or have it scraped by some rasping instrument until it is removed, and treat until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 of the limb which is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the fracture of the bone is healed, and afterwards the limb remains weak and delicate, this happens for many reasons: one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and the nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or from too great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, hence it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the cure is to make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until the blood increases in him; and administer baths, and give him joy and gladness; then apply pitch on the limb, so that the pitch draws great nourishment to it, and frequently wash it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 Of a twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are exposed, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one should break the limb all over again; and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great evils come from them, and sometimes death; however, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, then they must be softened with hot water, or softening herbs must be boiled, such as leaves of vismalva, and roots, and mellilot, and similar things; and you make a softening plaster, such as well-made diquilon, and you take the muscillaige of vismalva, and you cook it with goose grease or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or you take ripe figs, and grind them with colon flour, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continually and lengthily rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And there should be gentle movement of the limb each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the distortion is hardened and made hard like stone, and it needs to be removed with an iron tool, then it must be cut down to the bone, with a delicate incision gently; and put effort and study into the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation happens to someone, it must be immediately brought back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Because if one delays, the place swells, and perhaps one barely puts it back in its place; therefore, one should not move it when it is swollen: many times this brings on spasm and other pains; however, when this happens, have the patient bleed, then leave them until the abscess subsides; then wash the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each member as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It often happens that the jawbones are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are slightly removed from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated and hang downwards towards the chest, and saliva flows from the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and its tongue is wrapped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When a dislocation is small, it returns to its original place through various means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is whole and complete, it is necessary that you quickly reset it, and do not hesitate; and in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the doctor places his finger in one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and let the other two hands be free, to make it equal; and instruct the patient to soften their jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the doctor should place it evenly until it returns to its proper place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if it is difficult to return, whether it is the two jaws together, then raise them with hot water and oil, until you reset them lightly; do not hesitate in returning as we have said. xspace
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are returned equally, and the patient's mouth is closed well without softening, place wet bandages on a poultice made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft ligatures; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two cushions so that it does not move to the right or left, nor should they strain to speak, but let them eat light food until the pain is gone, and the jaws are bound; and then let them chew lightly what they want, and do not struggle to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be set right in one hour and are not returned to their places, then fever and hot fits ensue, and perhaps bellyache, and perhaps they will vomit pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, then know that it is fatal; and many times he who experiences it dies within IX days.
de la forcelle	 of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The fork cannot dislocate from the side inside the continuation of it and from the foot; and sometimes it is dislocated by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then press strongly on the place with your palm, and it will return; then apply the poultice and bandage, and bind it; and the head toward the side cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the poultice and the bandage, and bind it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus also is returned the shoulder blade when it is removed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is only dislocated in three ways: one way is that it dislocates towards the lower part of the armpit; and the second way is towards the ribs; and sometimes it dislocates upwards, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate backwards due to the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inward due to the nerves; and many times it dislocates downwards towards the armpit, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it quickly jumps; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And it happens to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and he thinks it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary for you to test it, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And know the dislocation when it is downward towards the scapula, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear diversity; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the scapula at the shoulder bone, just as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move any part of him; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly on the shoulder blade; and this manner of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the attendant takes the hand of the patient up high, then places his thumb under it, and lifts the joint with force upward to its place; and the attendant takes the hand, stretches it out high, then places it underneath; thus, it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in several days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the attendant should apply softening and soothing ointments, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be applied; then let the patient sit upright on his back, and place under the armpit a cloth of linen equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then let the physician place his heel on the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder firmly, and pull the hand of the patient; and another attendant holds the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; thus, the shoulder comes back immediately, and if you see it this way, you should reset it according to this manner: and it is that you make present a man who is larger than the patient; and he stands upright beside the patient's side, and places his shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lifts the armpit high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another attendant pulls the hand of the patient downward toward the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, have something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it is set back in another way: and this is how one drives a long log into the ground, so that its head is as round as a fist, neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but he should have soft blankets on top, and the patient should be standing along the length of the log; then his hand should be extended down from the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its place; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a log of two arms in length and four fingers in width, which has a round head so that it can easily enter deep under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then take the patient and place him on top of a board, wrapped in cloth so that the board does not hurt the patient. Then place it under the patient's bed; extend the arm along the length of the board, tie the shoulder to the board, and the arm at the wrist. Then place the arm on the rung of a wide ladder, with the hand hanging down, and let the body hang freely on the other side: now the joint will return into its place.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is in place, in whatever manner, you must put under the bed a flat piece of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with frankincense and egg white, over all the shoulder and around it. Then tightly bind it under the bed, turn the bandage over the plaster, encircle the hand around the neck, and let the hand remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he rest a little, until the member is comforted, for it will heal more quickly; and then let him rest more afterwards, one day or two, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three cauteries with holes, as it is stated in the chapter on cauteries before this one.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and he cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dislocation that is towards the foot and buttocks, or backside, is caused by a push and stretching of the hands, and another instrument is administered; treat it until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and delay in movement, let the patient take many baths, until that stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the hip
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the hip joint is dislocated by degrees, and returns by degrees; and if it has dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not obvious, because one can see and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each form.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick cut with the healthy one, you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is separated and the arm cannot bend nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And it is necessary that you reset it before an abscess forms there, because if an abscess forms there, the resetting will be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations, causing greater pain, and death may occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the resetting is such that when it can be reset, you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arm be spread out, and hold his hand according to the cut around, above and below, and push the joint together at its base, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm where it is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and it is that two assistants extend the arm, and hold it with two assistants, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth around it; and when the patient joins the joint to his hand, anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint very strongly, until it returns; and when it is in place, put on a dry poultice with egg white, and hold it firmly, and bind the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is firm in its place, then untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then tie the bandage again and leave it this way for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels stiffness after the return of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or place on the joint a greasy piece of mutton, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the mutton, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see, place a moist cow dung heated with butter on it, and bind it up; thus it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is slight, more than other joints However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it is dislocated, lest the place become swollen or an abscess form.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the return is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and the assistant extends his hand, and the doctor places it evenly, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns However, it must be seen if it is well in its place; then let the patient place the back of his hand on the table at the extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the healer places their hand on that part of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that is good; if not, then restrain it with soothing plasters for those abscesses, and leave it thus without recurrence.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains twisted; and nothing hurts the patient except that as long as the hand is wet, it cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is no other remedy except to cauterize near the case, and perhaps nothing else will help. 》
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, apply the plaster we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well, and there is some hardness, then moisten it with hot water, and rub until it softens.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated at each joint, sometimes at the back of the palm or in the hollow; then straighten the finger, and push the dislocation towards yourself until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and turn it toward the side where it is dislocated; and leave it for two days, and then set it equal on that day; and bind it with a nut, as we have said, and unbind after one day, and make it move, and rebind with a nut; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the palm of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and do the same when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the shoulder blade
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the shoulder blade or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign of this is that the exhalations jump out involuntarily, and he cannot hold them back, and often some members are softened, either both thighs or both arms or one, and often the shoulder blade moves in four parts; the part that moves to the rear is called "gibbosity": the cure for this is that you return it if the gibbosity is from childhood: there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from a fall or a blow or similar things, the ancients spoke of cures with great words, where there is not always great benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele qui vient droitement en II costez, and neither has any benefit nor health; and similarly that which comes straight to the two sides, cannot be cured except by that which comes specifically to the back, as I say; and it is necessary for the patient to be stretched on his face in an equal place, and have support under him so that he does not hurt himself. Then drive a stake into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie one cord around the ankles of the patient, and another at the hips, and the knees, and the ankles; and two assistants should know the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they should be well secured, the stakes as we have said, and the doctor should place his palms on the spine firmly, until it heals.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this cure, then take a board of three spans in length, and place it beneath the patient, who should be lying on their side, and push the head of the board under the patient, then place the middle of the board over the spine; and let the physician put his feet on the other end of the board, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do so for the shoulder that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And you should place two stakes at the head of the patient, one forearm's length apart, and towards the feet another two, with each stake separated by the width of a hand both above and below; and let there be a hole in each stake where the shoulder fits, and let the stakes be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move. And between each pair of stakes, let there be a turning stake on which the rope turns, and between the two turning stakes let there be two small stakes one hand's length long, to turn the shoulder; then tie the rope that is among the ashes to the shoulder towards the head, and the other rope to the other shoulder towards the feet, and each of the assistants turns his stake all the way along the rope, and the master aligns the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equalized, place an absorbent dressing with plenty of egg, then the bandages, and then a pad of three fingers' length, which should cover the area of jaundice and the healthy part of the vertebrae, then bind it with a ligature, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nourishment until healed; and if anything happens at the end of the healing, then administer softening and soothing medicines, with the pad that we mentioned before; and sometimes one administers a piece of lead, and sometimes it appears in the lower vertebrae of the back, and one thinks it is dislocation; and this is the bone that opens, which is why one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the joints of the hip and the shoulder, only dislocations occur, not as in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and it is more commonly dislocated inside than elsewhere, and rarely in front or behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 The sign of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the injured knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their knee; and the place next to it swells with an abscess because the head of the femur goes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the sign of this is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 And the sign of this is that he stretches his leg according to its length; however, do not bend the knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and the ankle swells, and when he walks, he walks on his heels.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the sign of this is that he cannot spread his knee, or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hipbone is in the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The treatment for this type of dislocation is that you wait if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no need for treatment; and it is not necessary for him to be impatient.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, which is one of the four kinds of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and pull it within and without, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return this way, then you must prepare a strong assistant, and pull the leg strongly with two hands, or bind a rope around the knee; and another assistant should place their hand above in such a manner that they push their hands under their armpits, then pull gently on the thigh with a soft rope; and another holds the end of the rope; and all stretch up and down at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	 Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 This manner of extension is common in four ways, and if the dislocation returns as we have said, that is good. If not, then one must care for its likeness. When the dislocation is on the outer side, you should place the patient on his healthy side, then put the ligature on the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the angle; then extend the ligature upwards towards the angle, and towards the groin. Then another assistant should take the arms of the patient, and embrace the thick part of the sick thigh, and stretch it firmly: thus it will return to its place now, and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot secure it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong, soft cord around the two ankles, and around the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him hang from the top of a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then instruct one assistant to embrace the thigh's head, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who embraces the thigh strongly, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.
