And when the dislocation is reduced, the patient lies down as we have said for someone with gout, and tighten the cord on the sick leg properly, and on the foot as well; then place two splints, one at the head and another at the feet, then insert a splint between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and let there be planted moist cloths around, that it may not hurt the patient, then each assistant extends towards him, and the surgeon sets the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place it on the table, and press it as we have said in the treatment of a dislocation, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly extend the injured leg, as I have said; and let the healer put his weight on the injured ankle, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is behind, one should not extend the injured leg downwards or lift it off the ground, but rather let it be as if the hip were dislocated behind, as we have said about lying on both hips; and he should be face up, and the ligament should be extended as we have said before, and someone should press on the joint at the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then bring the thighs together, and apply the plaster, and bind with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then unbind him, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, then bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind him, and let him walk well, until the limb is healed.  >
de la dislocation dou genoil	 Of the knee dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	 The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside and outside, and backward; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the sign is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it does not touch his thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your teeth, then strongly bend the two sides of the knee; and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it touches his thigh lightly; and apply a plaster, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and keep them together firmly for three days or four, then unbind; and the patient should not try to walk until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at all, then apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed
de la dislocation dou talon	 of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	 The ankles are sometimes swollen and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign is that the ankle is swollen and projects forward to the part where it is dislocated; the reduction is gentle, and one should extend it gently with their hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit up straight, and have two assistants hold onto the leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then towards the left two times, then raise it up high, and gently push the foot back up; and do this twice, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; but if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and firmly stick a peg in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloths around, so as not to hurt the patient; then let two assistants hold onto the thigh, and another assistant should support the foot with their hands or with a rope, which they tie around the ankle; then each assistant should pull equally, and the peg should always be between the patient’s thighs to keep the patient from moving when it is being pulled; then the physician should reset the dislocation with their own hands, and another assistant should hold onto the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will quickly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, apply the plaster and bandages on top, and bind very tightly, and tie the foot to the leg, and protect the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligament is not too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and if the ligament softens, bind again; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and prevent the patient from walking for four days; and if he walks before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess forms there, then you must calm it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	 of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	 When the two are dislocated, they must be properly extended without strain, and this is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any knot of the back of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat place or on a table completely straight, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press strongly with your foot until it returns; and when it is equal, and nothing appears there, then put under the sole of the foot a board with two legs, then hold it tightly, and leave it for three days, then unbind it; and make it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	 Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in this art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and compassionate and cautious, but bold; and at the beginning, use things to calm the abscess heat, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope of health there; and when you see hope, then reset the limb now, before the abscess comes there; and when the limb is set, then administer things to calm the abscess heat, and treat the wound as it should be with dry onions; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones have come out, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will help you according to your Creator, and because of the wisdom of your arms and body.
Amen	 Amen
